When Does Touching the Private Part Break Wudu? (Hanafi Ruling)
Ruling that touching the vulva with an erect penis without barrier breaks wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which touching the vulva with an erect penis nullifies wudu according to the Hanafi school, and explain the proofs cited.

Core Idea
Touching vulva with erect penis without barrier breaks wudu because it typically leads to madhi emission.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents a specific Hanafi ruling on a nullifier of wudu. It goes beyond general statements by defining three precise conditions: the male organ must be erect, there must be no barrier, and the action must be in a context leading to intercourse. The author further supports this ruling with multiple proofs including a hadith about touching the penis. Understanding this ruling helps avoid common mistakes about when wudu is broken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on the act of a man touching a woman's vulva with his erect penis without a barrier. The ruling: this action nullifies wudu (requires wudu).
2
List the three conditions
The text explicitly mentions three conditions: (1) the male organ is erect, (2) there is no barrier between the parts, (3) the nature of the touch is such that the next step is intercourse.
These conditions are specific to the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the rationale
The author explains that this action typically leads to the emission of madhi (pre-ejaculatory fluid), which is a nullifier of wudu. Thus, the ruling is placed in the category of fluid exit, similar to deep sleep being placed in the category of wind exit.
This is a qiyas based on the usual consequence.
4
Examine the proofs
The text cites multiple proofs: (1) Athar from Ibn Mas'ud about direct contact requiring wudu, (2) Hadith from Abu Huraira about touching without barrier, (3) Athar from Ibrahim about kissing/lust, and (4) a mention that other scholars (Shafi'i) require wudu even from touching the penis alone.
The Hanafi school uses these to support their position.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that any touching of the private part (either sex) with desire breaks wudu; without desire it does not. The Hanafi position is more specific, requiring the three conditions.
The practical difference: a man touching his own penis without erection does not break wudu in Hanafi, but does in Shafi'i if with desire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۳) ومس فرج بذكر منتصب بلا حائل.
ترجمه : (۱۴۳) (۱۲) اور بغیر کسی حائل کے کھڑے ہوئے ذکر کا شرمگاہ سے چھونا۔
تشریح : یہاں تین باتیں ہیں [1] مرد کا عضو تناسل کھڑا ہے [۲] مرد اور عورت کے عضو خاص کے درمیان کوئی چیز حائل نہیں ہے - [۳] مرد اس طرح شرمگاہ سے مس کر رہا ہے کہ اگلا مرحلہ جماع کا ہے، ایسی صورت میں عام طور پر جب مرد کا عضو سکڑتا ہے تو اس سے مذی خارج ہو جاتی ہے، اس لئے ایسا کرنے کو ہی ندی نکلنے کے درجے میں رکھ کر وضو ٹوڑنے کا حکم لگا دیا گیا ، جس طرح گہری نیند کو ہوا نکلنے کے درجے میں رکھ دی گئی۔
وجه : (1) اس اثر میں ہے۔ ان ابن مسعود قال : يتوضأ الرجل من المباشرة ، و من اللمس بيده ، و من القبلة اذا قبل امراته و كان يقول في هذه الآية او لامستم النساء - آیت ۴۳ ،سورة النساء ) قال هو الغمز - ) مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الوضوء من القبلة والمس والمباشرة ، ج اول ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۴۹۹) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ مباشرت سے وضو واجب ہے (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه من افضى بيده الى فرجه ليس دونها حجاب فقد وجب عليه وضوء الصلاة . (سنن بیہقی ، باب ترک الوضوء من مس الفرج بظهر الكف ، ج اول ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۶۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بغیر حجاب کے فرج چھو یا تو وضو واجب ہے۔ (۳) عن ابراهیم قال اذا قبل الرجل بشهوة او لمس بشهوة فعليه الوضوء - (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الوضوء من القبلة والمس والمباشرة ، ج اول ص ۱۰۲، نمبر ۵۰۱) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ عورت کو بوسہ لینے کے بعد وضو کرے۔ (۴) دوسرے حضرات تو صرف مس ذکر سے بھی وضو لازم کرتے ہیں، اور یہاں میں ذکر ہوگا اس لئے بھی وضو واجب ہونا چاہئے ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه اذا مس احدكم ذكره فعليه الوضوء - ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الوضوء من مس الذکر ص ۶۸ نمبر ۴۸۰ [سنن] ابوداود شریف ، باب الوضوء من مس الذکر ص ۳۶ نمبر (۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مس ذکر سے وضو ہے۔
لغت : مس: چھونا، رگڑنا۔ فرج: عورت کی شرمگاہ ۔ منتصب : ایستادہ، کھڑا ۔ حائل: درمیان کا پردہ۔
(143) And touching the vulva with an erect penis without a barrier. Translation: (143) (12) And touching the private part (of a woman) with an erect penis without any barrier. Explanation: There are three matters: [1] The man's penis is erect. [2] There is no barrier between the man's and woman's private parts. [3] The man is touching in such a way that the next step is intercourse. In this case, generally when the man's organ shrinks, pre-ejaculatory fluid (madhi) comes out. Therefore, this action is placed in the category of fluid exit, and the ruling of breaking wudu is applied, just as deep sleep is placed in the category of wind exit. Proofs: (1) Athar from Ibn Mas'ud... (2) Hadith from Abu Huraira... (3) Athar from Ibrahim... (4) Other scholars make wudu necessary even from touching the penis, and here the penis is involved, so wudu is also obligatory. Hadith from Jabir... Vocabulary: mas: touching, rubbing. farj: woman's private part. muntasib: erect, standing. ha'il: barrier, covering in between.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This is a ruling with multiple proofs. The Hanafi school takes a specific position: touching the vulva with an erect penis without a barrier nullifies wudu, because this action typically leads to the emission of madhi (pre-ejaculate), which is a nullifier. The text conditions three factors: erection, no barrier, and proximity to intercourse. The proofs include athar from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibrahim, as well as a hadith from Abu Huraira about touching the private part without a barrier. Additionally, the author notes that if simply touching the penis (without erection or female genitalia) requires wudu according to other scholars, then a fortiori this case requires wudu. This ruling is an application of the principle of considering the usual consequence (ghalabat al-hal). The vocabulary clarifies the key terms.

Key Terms
فرج (farj): The female private part (vulva)
منتصب (muntasib): Erect (of the male organ)
حائل (ha'il): Barrier or covering between the touching parts
مذی (madhi): Pre-ejaculatory fluid, considered a nullifier of wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in the text, under what condition does touching the female private part with the male organ break wudu?
A) Any touching with or without barrier
B) Touching with an erect penis and without a barrier
C) Touching only if it leads to actual intercourse
D) Touching only if done intentionally

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines wudu nullification from touching based on the likely emission of madhi, requiring three specific conditions.

Touching Genitals with an Erect Penis Nullifies Wudu
Ruling on nullification of wudu by touching genitals with erect penis without barrier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nullification of wudu by touching genitals, identify the conditions (erect penis, no barrier), and cite the key hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Touching genitals nullifies wudu only if the penis is erect and there is no barrier.

This passage addresses a specific nullifier of wudu: touching the female genitals with an erect penis without a barrier. The Hanafi school distinguishes this case from other types of touch, emphasizing the conditions that trigger nullification. The author provides four proofs from the Salaf to support the ruling. Understanding these conditions is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its conditions
The act is mass farj (touching genitals) with an erect penis (muntasib) and no barrier (la ha'il).
These conditions are explicitly stated in the Arabic: 'bizakarin muntasib bila ha'il'.
2
State the ruling
This act nullifies wudu. The passage implies that after such touch, one must perform wudu again before prayer.
3
Locate the dalil
The passage cites four proofs: (1) statement of Ibn Mas'ud, (2) hadith of Abu Hurairah, (3) saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, (4) hadith of Jabir.
The hadith from Abu Hurairah is the primary evidence with explicit wording.
4
Analyze the main hadith
The hadith: 'Whoever places his hand on his own private part without a barrier, then wudu for prayer becomes obligatory upon him.' This directly indicates nullification of previous wudu.
The phrase 'wajaba alayhi wudu al-salah' is the key operative phrase (wajh al-dalalah).
5
Note the Hanafi specificity
The condition 'erect penis' is inferred from the context of desire and likelihood of emission of madhiy (pre-ejaculatory fluid), which is a known nullifier. If the penis is flaccid or a barrier exists, wudu is not nullified.
This differentiates the Hanafi position from other schools that may nullify wudu upon any touch without barrier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في نواقض الوضوء ولو تعمّد الخروج بها من الصلوة (١٤٣) ومس فرج بذكر منتصب بلا حائل. وجه: (١) عن ابن مسعود قال: يتوضأ الرجل من المباشرة، ومن اللمس بيده، ومن القبلة اذا قبل امراته وكان يقول في هذه الآية أو لامستم النساء (النساء: ٤٣) قال هو الغمز. (٢) عن أبي هريرة قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من أفضى بيده إلى فرجه ليس دونها حجاب فقد وجب عليه وضوء الصلاة. (٣) عن إبراهيم قال: اذا قبل الرجل بشهوة أو لمس بشهوة فعليه الوضوء. (٤) عن جابر بن عبد الله قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: اذا مس أحدكم ذكره فعليه الوضوء.
Section on Nullifiers of Wudu: And if he intentionally exits from prayer (143) and touching the genitals (of a woman) with an erect penis without a barrier. Evidence: (1) From Ibn Mas'ud: A man performs wudu from direct contact, from touching with his hand, and from kissing when he kisses his wife, and he used to say regarding this verse 'or you have touched women' (4:43) – he said: it means fondling. (2) From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever places his hand on his own private part without a barrier, then wudu for prayer becomes obligatory upon him. (3) From Ibrahim: When a man kisses with desire or touches with desire, then wudu is upon him. (4) From Jabir ibn Abdullah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When any of you touches his penis, then wudu is upon him.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the section on nullifiers of wudu. It specifically addresses touching the genitals of a woman with an erect penis without a barrier. The ruling is that wudu is nullified. The underlying reason, explained in the Urdu commentary (not in the Arabic clean), is that such an act typically leads to the emission of madhiy (pre-ejaculatory fluid), which is a known nullifier. The author then provides four proofs: (1) the statement of Ibn Mas'ud that wudu is required from direct contact (mubasharah) and kissing; (2) a hadith from Abu Hurairah stating that touching one's own private part without a barrier necessitates wudu; (3) the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that kissing or touching with desire requires wudu; (4) a hadith from Jabir that touching the penis requires wudu. These evidences establish the Hanafi position that such touching nullifies wudu.

Key Terms
مس فرج (mass farj): Touching the genitals (specifically of a woman) with the hand or penis.
منتصب (muntasib): Erect (penis), a condition for nullification in this ruling.
حائل (ha'il): Barrier covering the private part, such as clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) When the touch is with the back of the hand
D) When the person is in a state of janabah

Key Takeaway
Touching genitals nullifies wudu only when the penis is erect and there is no barrier.

What Does Not Nullify Wudu: The Ten Exceptions
Listing of ten nullifiers exceptions with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten things that do not nullify wudu and explain why non-flowing blood does not nullify, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Only flowing blood nullifies wudu; non-flowing blood and similar discharges do not break ablution.

This lesson addresses a common confusion: when does blood or discharge actually nullify wudu? The Hanafi school provides a clear criterion—only flowing blood nullifies. We will explore a hadith and a companion statement that establish this principle, and then list the full set of ten exceptions that do not require renewing wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of rulings
Recognize that the text lists exceptions: these items do NOT nullify wudu. Understand that nullifiers are covered elsewhere; here we highlight what is not a nullifier.
The list serves as a practical guide to avoid unnecessary repetitions of wudu.
2
Examine the proof for non-flowing blood
Read the hadith from Abu Hurairah and the statement of 'Ata. Note that the exception 'unless it is flowing blood' implies that non-flowing blood does not necessitate wudu.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Daraqutni and is ahad, but accepted in Hanafi school.
3
Apply the principle to analogous cases
By analogy, pus, non-flowing blood from a wound, and similar discharges also do not nullify. The key illa (effective cause) is the absence of flow.
The Hanafi school extends the ruling to all non-flowing impurities from the body.
4
Memorize the full list
The ten items are enumerated: non-flowing blood, fallen flesh without blood, non-flowing pus, touching genitals, touching a woman, vomit less than mouthful, phlegm, three types of sleep. Commit them to memory.
Use mnemonic devices if helpful; the list is frequently tested in fiqh exams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : (عشرة اشياء لا ينقض الوضوء) (١٤٤) ظهور دم لم يسل عن محله (١٤٥) وسقوط لحم من غير سيلان دم كالعرق المدني الذي [ثم سرد باللغة الأردية: عشر أشياء لا تنقض الوضوء: ١. ظهور دم لم يسل، ٢. سقوط لحم بلا سيلان كالعرق المدني، ٣. خروج قيح من جرح وأذن وأنف، ٤. مس الذكر، ٥. مس المرأة، ٦. قيء بلا ملء الفم، ٧. قيء بلغم وإن كثر، ٨. نوم النائم بحيث يحتمل زوال مقعده عن الأرض، ٩. نوم على الأرض مع الإقعاء، ١٠. نوم المصلي ولو في ركوع وسجود على الطريقة المسنونة.] وجه: (١) عن أبي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: ليس في القطرة والقطرتين من الدم وضوء إلا أن يكون دماً سائلاً. (٢) عن عطاء في الشجة: إن سال الدم فليتوضأ، وإن ظهر ولم يسل فلا وضوء عليه.
Section: Ten things that do not nullify wudu: (144) Appearance of blood that did not flow from its place; (145) Falling of flesh without blood flow, like the 'urq madani (a thread-like growth). [Then listed in Urdu: Ten things that do not nullify wudu: 1. Appearance of blood that did not flow; 2. Falling of flesh without blood flow, like a thread; 3. Pus exiting from wound, ear, nose; 4. Touching the penis; 5. Touching a woman; 6. Vomiting without filling the mouth; 7. Vomiting phlegm even if much; 8. Sleeping of a person such that there is a possibility of his buttocks losing contact with the ground; 9. Sleeping on the ground with the buttocks encircled; 10. Sleeping of a praying person even if in ruku' and sujud in the sunnah manner.] Evidence: (1) From Abu Hurairah from the Prophet (peace be upon him): There is no wudu required from one or two drops of blood unless it is flowing blood. (2) From 'Ata regarding a head wound: If blood flows, then let him perform wudu; but if it appears and does not flow, then no wudu is required.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This section lists ten things that do not nullify wudu, serving as exceptions to the nullifiers. The Arabic text explicitly mentions the first two: non-flowing blood and falling flesh without blood; the Urdu commentary completes the list. The key principle is that only flowing blood (dam sail) nullifies wudu, not mere appearance. The evidence provided distinguishes between flowing and non-flowing blood, citing a hadith from Abu Hurairah and a statement from 'Ata. The Hanafi school adheres to this distinction. The list also clarifies that touching the genitals (of oneself or a woman) does not nullify wudu per se — though earlier rulings specify conditions under which it does nullify (e.g., with erect penis and no barrier). This demonstrates the nuanced approach of the madhhab.

Key Terms
دم سائل (dam sail): Flowing blood; blood that runs from its place.
عرق مدني (urq madani): A thin flesh-like growth resembling a thread (often called 'granulation tissue' or 'proud flesh').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Only flowing blood or discharges nullify wudu; non-flowing substances do not.

Ten Things That Do Not Break Wudu: Hanafi Rulings and Proofs
Lists ten items that do not nullify wudu with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten things that do not break wudu according to the Hanafi school, explain the Hanafi evidence for each, and distinguish between nullifiers and non-nullifiers.

Core Idea
Only flowing blood and matter exiting the front/back passages break wudu; touch and non-flowing blood do not.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on ten specific actions that do not nullify wudu. Although wudu is required for prayer, knowing what does not break it is essential for daily practice. We will explore the evidence from hadith and the reasoning behind each exception, particularly the distinction between flowing blood and mere contact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first item: blood that does not flow
Note the condition: the blood must appear but not flow from its place. This is the key distinction – only 'dam masfuh' (flowing blood) breaks wudu.
Hanafi rely on the hadith of Ibn Umar squeezing a pimple without renewing wudu.
2
Identify the second item: falling flesh without blood flow
Like the 'Irq Madani disease where a fleshy growth falls without bleeding. Wudu remains intact because no flowing impurity exits.
Assessed by analogy to the first item.
3
Identify the third item: worm from wound, ear, or nose
If the worm exits from the front or back passage, it breaks wudu. But from other places, if no flowing blood accompanies it, wudu is not broken.
Analogy to falling flesh; the worm carries little impurity.
4
Identify the fourth and fifth items: touching penis and touching woman
These do not break wudu because no impurity exits. The Prophet's statement and action serve as proof.
Hanafi evidence: 'Is it not merely a piece of flesh?' and kissing Aisha without renewing wudu.
5
Compare with the opposing Shafi'i view
The Shafi'i school holds that touching the private part or a woman (with desire) breaks wudu. The practical difference is whether one must renew wudu after such contact.
Hanafis do not renew; Shafi'is do.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في ما لا ينقض الوضوع
فصل : (عشرة اشياء لا ينقض الوضوء)
(۱۴۴) ظهور دم لم يسل عن محله (۱۴۵) وسقوط لحم من غير سيلان دم كالعرق المدني الذي يقال له رشته (۱۴۶) وخروج دودة من جرح واذن وانف (۱۴۷) ومس ذکر و مس امرأة تشریح : بہتا ہوا خون ناقض وضو ہے، اس لئے اگر خون بہے بغیر گوشت کا ٹکڑا کٹ کر گر جائے تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ جیسے عرق مدنی ، ایک بیماری ہے، جسکو فارسی میں رشتہ کہتے ہیں، اس میں گوشت کا ٹکڑا کٹ کر گرتا ہے، اور خون نہیں بہتا، اس لئے اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۶) (۳) اور زخم اور کان اور ناک سے کیڑے کا نکلنا۔
تشریح : پیخانہ اور پیشاب کے راستے سے کیڑا نکلے تو اس سے وضوٹوٹ جائے گا، کیونکہ تھوڑی سے چیز بھی وہاں سے نکلے تو اس سے وضوٹوٹ جاتا ہے۔ لیکن ان دونوں کے علاوہ سے [ مثلا زخم سے یا کان ناک سے] کیڑا نکلے تو اس پر تھوڑا سا خون یا نا پا کی ہے، جو دم مسفوح نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا ، جیسے گوشت بغیر خون کے کٹ کر گرے تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹتا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) وقال طاؤس ، و مـحـمـد ابن علی و عطاء و اهل الحجاز ليس في الدم وضوء ، و عصر ابن عمر بثرة فخرج منها الدم و لم يتوضاً ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب من لم ير الوضوء الامن المحمر جين من القبل والد بر ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۱۷۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ خون نکلنے میں وضو نہیں ہے، جس کا مطلب یہ لیا جا سکتا ہے کہ سبیلین کے علاوہ سے ہوا اور دم مسفوح نہ تو لی ہو تو وضو نہیں ہے۔ (۲) قال لي عطاء توضأ من كل دم خرج فسال ، قيح او دمل او نقطة يسيرة اذا خرج فسال فيه الوضوء قال و ان نزعت سنا فسال منها دم فتوضاً ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الوضوء من الدم ، ج اول ص 111 نمبر ۵۴۶ ) اس اثر میں بھی ہے کہ خون بہے تب وضوٹوٹے گا ورنہ نہیں ، اور یہاں کیڑے پر بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
ترجمه : (۱۴۷) [۴] اور ذکر کا چھونا۔ [۵] اور عورت کا چھوٹا۔ تشریح : اصول یہ ہے کہ جسم سے نجاست نکلنے سے وضو ٹوٹتا ہے ذکر کے چھونے سے عورت کے چھونے سے مذی وغیرہ کوئی نجاست نہیں نکلی تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ دوسرے حضرات کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ ذکر چھونے سے ، اور عورت کو چھونے سے وضو ٹوٹے گا ، حنفیہ کا مسلک یہ نہیں ہے۔
وجه : (۱) عن قيس بن طلق عن ابيه قال قدمنا على نبي الله له فجاء رجل كانه بدوی فقال یا نبی الله ! ما ترى مس الرجل ذكره بعد ما يتوضأ ، فقال هل هو الا مضغة منه او بضعة منه (ابوداود شریف، باب الرخصة فی ذالک ،ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۱۸۲ را ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب الرخصة فی ذالک، ص ۱۹، نمبر ۴۸۳ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مس ذکر سے وضو لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ (۲) عن عائشة ان النبى ال اللي قبلها و لم يتوضأ ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب الوضوء من القبلة ، ص ۱۳۶، نمبر
Chapter on what does not break wudu: Ten things do not break wudu: (144) Appearance of blood that does not flow from its place; (145) falling of flesh without blood flow, like the 'Irq Madani which is called 'rishta'; (146) exit of a worm from a wound, ear, or nose; (147) touching the penis and touching a woman. Explanation: Flowing blood breaks wudu, but if a piece of flesh falls without blood, wudu is not broken. Like 'Irq Madani, a disease where a piece of flesh falls without blood. (3) And exit of a worm from a wound, ear, or nose. Explanation: If a worm exits from the front or back passage, wudu breaks because any small thing from there breaks it. But from elsewhere, as the worm has little blood or impurity that is not flowing, wudu is not broken. Evidence: (1) Tawus, Muhammad ibn Ali, Ata, and the people of Hijaz said: No wudu from blood; Ibn Umar squeezed a pimple and blood came out and he did not perform wudu. (2) Ata said: Perform wudu from every blood that comes out and flows; if it does not flow, no wudu. (4) Touching the penis; (5) touching a woman. Explanation: The principle is that wudu breaks due to impurity exiting the body; touching the penis or a woman does not cause impurity to exit. Other schools hold that touching breaks wudu, but the Hanafi school does not. Evidence: (1) The Prophet said: The penis is only a piece of flesh. (2) The Prophet kissed Aisha and did not perform wudu.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school concerning what does not break wudu. It lists ten specific things, though only five are detailed here. The first is blood that appears but does not flow from its place—this does not break wudu because the nullifying agent is flowing blood (dam masfuh). The Hadith cited (from al-Daraqutni) explicitly states that two drops of blood do not break wudu unless it is flowing. The second is the falling of flesh without blood, such as in the disease 'Irq Madani (a fleshy growth). Since no flowing blood accompanies it, wudu remains intact. The third is the exit of a worm from a wound, ear, or nose. Worms from the front or back passages break wudu because any matter from those passages nullifies it, but from other sites, if the worm does not carry flowing blood, it does not break wudu, analogously to falling flesh. The fourth and fifth are touching the penis and touching a woman. The Hanafi position is that such touching does not break wudu because no impurity exits; touching alone is not a cause. The opposing school (Shafi'i) holds that touching breaks wudu, but the Hanafi school relies on the Hadith from Qays ibn Talq that the penis is merely a piece of flesh, and the practice of the Prophet kissing Aisha without renewal of wudu.

Key Terms
دم مسفوح (dam masfuh): Blood that flows out of its place, which nullifies wudu.
مس ذکر (mass dhakar): Touching the male private part with the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following does NOT break wudu?
A) A worm exiting from the front passage
B) Flowing blood from a wound
C) Touching one's own private part
D) Vomiting a mouthful

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, only the exit of impurity (especially flowing blood or matter from the private parts) breaks wudu; mere contact or non-flowing blood does not.

Touching the Penis or a Woman Does Not Nullify Wudu
Ruling on touching one's own penis or a woman not breaking wudu with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching the penis or a woman, explain the dalil, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Wudu breaks by exiting impurity, not by touch; the penis is just a piece of flesh.

This passage addresses a common question about what nullifies wudu. The Hanafi school holds that touching one's own penis or a woman does not break wudu, contrary to the Shafi'i school. The proofs are from hadith, which we will examine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Principle
The principle is that wudu breaks only when impurity exits the body. Touching does not release impurity.
This is the foundational rule.
2
Locate the Ruling
The ruling is that touching the penis or a woman does not nullify wudu.
Direct statement from the text.
3
Examine the Dalil
The Prophet said: 'Is it but a piece of flesh?' indicating that touching it does not require wudu. Also, the Prophet kissed Aisha without wudu.
Hadith from Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that touching the penis or a woman with desire nullifies wudu.
Their main evidence is a different hadith.
5
Understand Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practically, a Hanafi can touch without renewing wudu; a Shafi'i must renew wudu after such touch.
This is the practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۴۷) [۴] اور ذکر کا چھونا۔ [۵] اور عورت کا چھوٹا۔ تشریح : اصول یہ ہے کہ جسم سے نجاست نکلنے سے وضو ٹوٹتا ہے ذکر کے چھونے سے عورت کے چھونے سے مذی وغیرہ کوئی نجاست نہیں نکلی تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ دوسرے حضرات کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ ذکر چھونے سے ، اور عورت کو چھونے سے وضو ٹوٹے گا ، حنفیہ کا مسلک یہ نہیں ہے۔
وجه : (۱) عن قيس بن طلق عن ابيه قال قدمنا على نبي الله له فجاء رجل كانه بدوی فقال یا نبی الله ! ما ترى مس الرجل ذكره بعد ما يتوضأ ، فقال هل هو الا مضغة منه او بضعة منه (ابوداود شریف، باب الرخصة فی ذالک ،ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۱۸۲ را ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب الرخصة فی ذالک، ص ۱۹، نمبر ۴۸۳ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مس ذکر سے وضو لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ (۲) عن عائشة ان النبى ال اللي قبلها و لم يتوضأ ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب الوضوء من القبلة ، ص ۱۳۶، نمبر
Translation: (147) [4] And touching the penis. [5] And touching a woman. Explanation: The principle is that wudu breaks due to impurity exiting the body. From touching the penis or touching a woman, no impurity like madhi exits, so wudu does not break. The opinion of other scholars is that touching the penis and touching a woman break wudu; the Hanafi position is not that. Proof: (1) From Qays ibn Talq from his father: We came to the Prophet of Allah, and a man who looked like a bedouin came and said: O Prophet of Allah, what do you say about a man touching his penis after he performs wudu? He said: Is it but a piece of flesh from him? (Abu Dawud, Chapter on concession in that, p. 136, no. 182; Ibn Majah, Chapter on concession in that, p. 19, no. 483) This hadith indicates that touching the penis does not necessitate wudu. (2) From Aisha that the Prophet kissed her and did not perform wudu. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on wudu from kissing, p. 136, no.)
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding touching the penis and touching a woman. The author first states the Hanafi principle: wudu breaks only due to impurity exiting the body. Touching does not release impurity, so wudu remains valid. He then mentions that other scholars (such as the Shafi'i school) hold that touching the penis or a woman with desire breaks wudu. The Hanafi school rejects this. The proofs provided are two hadith: one from Talq ibn Ali that the Prophet said the penis is just a piece of flesh, so touching it does not break wudu; and another from Aisha that the Prophet kissed her without renewing wudu. These support the Hanafi position that touching does not nullify wudu.

Key Terms
مس ذکر (mass al-dhakar): Touching one's own penis with the hand.
مس امرأة (mass al-mar'ah): Touching a woman (with or without desire, depending on school).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does wudu break if a man touches his own penis without any impurity?
A) Yes, because touching private parts requires wudu.
B) No, because it is just a piece of flesh.
C) Yes, because it is similar to exiting impurity.
D) No, but only if he does not have desire.

Key Takeaway
Touching the penis or a woman does not nullify wudu in Hanafi school because nullification occurs only by exiting impurity.

Vomit Less Than a Mouthful Does Not Nullify Wudu
Ruling with dalil on quantity of vomit nullifying wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vomit quantity and nullification of wudu, and apply the distinction between little and much based on the athar.

Core Idea
Only a mouthful of vomit breaks wudu; less is overlooked.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on vomiting and its effect on wudu. The source passage establishes that only a significant amount — defined as a mouthful — nullifies wudu, while less than that is excused. This is based on an athar from Hammad, a notable early jurist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage to determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm is: vomiting less than a mouthful does not break wudu.
The ruling is specific to nullification of wudu.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from Hammad. Find the exact quote and its source (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf Abdurrazzaq).
The dalil is a qawl of a tabi'i, which in Hanafi usul can be used as evidence.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the athar prove the ruling? Hammad explicitly distinguishes between little (yasir) and much (kathir) regurgitation: little requires no wudu, much requires wudu. This indicates that the quantity is the decisive factor.
The word 'qalas' refers to regurgitation, but the same ruling applies to vomit (qay') in the Hanafi school.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may hold that any vomit, regardless of quantity, nullifies wudu. Recognize that this is a point of difference (mukhtalaf fih).
The Hanafi position is based on the athar and istihsan.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that only a mouthful or more nullifies. This is the relied-upon view in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah, so it is a strong position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۴۸) (۶) اور منہ بھر سے کم قے کرنا۔
تشریح : منہ بھر کرتے ہو تو اوپر گزرا کہ وضو ٹوٹے گا ، اور منہ بھر کر نہ ہو تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
وجه : عن حماد في القلس اذا كان يسيرا فليس فيه وضوء ، واذا كان كثيرا ففيه الوضوء ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، ۴۹ من کان یری فی الفلس وضوء ، ج اول ص ۴۵، نمبر ۴۴۲ مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب الوضوء من القيء والقلس ، ج اول ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۵۱۸) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ قے منہ بھر سے کم ہو تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
Translation: (148) (6) And vomiting less than a mouthful. Explanation: If it fills the mouth, as passed earlier, wudu breaks; if it does not fill the mouth, wudu does not break. Proof: From Hammad regarding regurgitation (qalas): if it is little, there is no wudu from it; if it is much, there is wudu from it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol. 1, p. 45, no. 442; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, vol. 1, p. 105, no. 518) This athar also indicates that if vomit is less than a mouthful, wudu does not break.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding the quantity of vomit that nullifies wudu. The author states that if the vomit is less than a mouthful, wudu does not break. The proof is an athar from Hammad, who distinguishes between little and much regurgitation. The Hanafi school considers that only a mouthful of vomit (from the stomach) nullifies wudu, because it is considered significant impurity. A smaller amount is overlooked (ma'fu).

Key Terms
قلس (qalas): Regurgitation of stomach contents; vomit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Does wudu break if a person vomits a small amount that does not fill the mouth?
A) Yes, because vomiting always breaks wudu.
B) No, because it is less than a mouthful.
C) Yes, because it comes from the stomach.
D) No, but only if it is not from food.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that only a mouthful of vomit nullifies wudu; lesser amounts are overlooked.

Vomiting Phlegm: A Unique Hanafi Ruling on Wudu Nullification
Ruling on phlegm vomit not breaking wudu regardless of amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vomiting phlegm and explain the rationale that distinguishes it from vomiting food.

Core Idea
Phlegm vomit does not break wudu because impurity is tied to stomach contents, not head/throat.

This lesson examines a specific and oft-misunderstood ruling: the nullification of wudu by vomiting. While a mouthful of food vomit invalidates wudu, the Hanafi school rules that phlegm, even in abundance, does not. The distinction lies in the source of impurity—phlegm originates in the respiratory tract, not the stomach. We will explore the textual proof from the companion Ata and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is vomiting phlegm. According to the Hanafi school, it does not break wudu, even if it fills the mouth.
This contrasts with vomiting food, which does break wudu if a mouthful.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar (saying) of the companion Ata, recorded in Musannaf Abdurrazzaq (no. 518).
The athar explicitly states that only stomach contents require wudu.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key part: 'except what comes out of your stomach from your belly.' This exception implies that non-stomach matter (like phlegm) does not necessitate wudu.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other madhhabs (e.g., Shafi'i) generally consider any mouthful vomit, including phlegm, as nullifying wudu.
The disagreement stems from different interpretations of the general rule about vomiting.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by the athar of Ata. It is the mufta bihi position.
The rationale (tahsin) that phlegm lacks stomach impurity further strengthens the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۴۹) [۷] اور بلغم کی تے ،اگر چہ زیادہ ہو۔
تشریح : کھانے کی قے منہ بھر کر ہو تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا لیکن بلغم کی تے منہ بھر کر ہو تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ وجه : (۱) کھانے میں پیٹ کی نجاست لگی ہوتی ہے لیکن بلغم چکنا ہوتا ہے اور عموما سر میں ہوتا ہے یا حلق میں ہے جہاں نجاست نہیں ہے اس لئے بلغم کی قے منہ بھر کر ہو تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا، کیونکہ اس میں نجاست نہیں ہے ۔ (۲) اس قول صحابی میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ قلت لعطاء.... قال لعمرى ! انى لانتخم شيئا كثيرا ثم يأتى الشيء من حلقى و من الرأس فليس فی ذالک وضوء الا ما خرج من جوفك من معدتک ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الوضوء من القى ، والفلس ، ج اول ص ۱۰۵ نمبر (۵۱۸) اس میں ہے کہ بلغم ہو تو وضو نہیں ہے۔
Translation: (149) [7] And vomiting phlegm, even if much. Explanation: Vomit of food, if it fills the mouth, wudu breaks; but vomiting phlegm, even if it fills the mouth, wudu does not break. Proof: (1) Food has stomach impurity attached, but phlegm is slimy and generally originates in the head or throat where there is no impurity. Therefore, vomiting phlegm even if a mouthful does not break wudu because there is no impurity in it. (2) This is proven by the saying of a companion: I said to Ata... He said: By my life, I expel much phlegm, then something comes from my throat and head; there is no wudu in that except what comes out of your stomach from your belly. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Chapter on wudu from vomit and regurgitation, vol. 1, p. 105, no. 518) This indicates that phlegm does not require wudu.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding vomiting phlegm. The author clarifies that phlegm, even in large quantity (a mouthful), does not nullify wudu, unlike food vomit. The reason given is that phlegm is not from the stomach but from the head/throat, so it is not impure like stomach contents. The proof is an athar from Ata, who states that only what comes from the stomach requires wudu; phlegm from the head does not. This is a distinctive Hanafi ruling based on the source of the impurity.

Key Terms
بلغم (balgham): Phlegm; mucus from the respiratory tract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Does wudu break if a person vomits a mouthful of phlegm?
A) Yes, because it is a mouthful.
B) No, because phlegm is from the head, not the stomach, and is not impure.
C) Yes, because vomiting always breaks wudu.
D) No, but only if it is less than a mouthful.

Key Takeaway
Phlegm vomit does not break wudu because it originates from the head/throat, not the stomach, and is not impure—a distinctive Hanafi ruling based on the athar of Ata.

Light Sleep Does Not Nullify Wudu: The Hanafi Criterion of the Anus Remaining on the Ground
Ruling with proof on light sleep not breaking wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion for distinguishing light sleep from deep sleep regarding wudu nullification—specifically, that as long as the anus remains on the ground, wudu is not broken even if the sleeping person moves.

Core Idea
Deep sleep (loss of intellect) breaks wudu; light sleep does not, even if the body moves, as long as the anus stays on the ground.

This lesson examines a precise Hanafi ruling about sleep and wudu. Not all sleep nullifies wudu; only deep sleep that fully removes consciousness and relaxes the joints does. The key indicator is whether the sleeping person's anus remains on the ground—if it does, the sleep is considered light and wudu remains valid. This distinction is based on a hadith from Tirmidhi and is a hallmark of Hanafi precision in taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is light sleep where the anus does not leave the ground. The ruling is that this type of sleep does not nullify wudu.
The opposite, deep sleep (lying down, joints relaxed), does break wudu.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'Indeed, wudu is only obligatory upon one who sleeps lying down, because when he lies down, his joints relax.' (Tirmidhi, no. 77).
The hadith is an ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith links wudu obligation to lying down (deep sleep) causing joint relaxation. Light sleep, where joints are not fully relaxed and the anus stays on the ground, does not meet this condition, so no wudu is required.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr bi al-shay' nahy 'an diddih? Actually the hadith specifies a condition for nullification.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school generally considers any sleep that removes consciousness as nullifying wudu. The Hanafi school restricts nullification to deep sleep.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of the same or different hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and is supported by the explicit hadith. It is part of Zahir al-Riwayah and relied upon in fatwa.
The authority is zahir_riwayah and the hadith is from Tirmidhi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۵۰) [۸] سونے والا اتنا ہلنے لگا کہ اس کی مقعد زائل ہونے کا احتمال ہو۔ تشریح : آگے کے تینوں مسئلوں میں اصول یہ ہے کہ اتنی گہری نیند ہو کہ معقل زائل ہوگئی ہو تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا، اور ہلکی نیند ہو کہ ابھی عقل زائل نہیں ہوئی ہے تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ کیونکہ معقل زائل ہونے کے بعد ہی تمام اعضاء ڈھیلے ہو جاتے ہیں، اور آدمی کو پتہ نہیں چلتا کہ ہو انکلی ہے یا نہیں اس لئے گہری نیند کے سونے کو ہی ہوا نکلنے کے درجے میں رکھ کر وضو ٹوٹنے کا حکم لگا دیا گیا ہے ۔ آگے کے تینوں مسئلوں میں ابھی گہری نیند نہیں ہے اسی لئے مسئلہ نمبر ۸] میں ہے کہ جھونکا کھانے لگا ہے لیکن مقعد زمین سے نہیں اٹھی یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ ابھی نیند ہلکی ہے، اس لئے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ اگر اس بات کا یقین ہو جائے کہ مقعد زمین سے
اٹھ چکی ہے تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا
وجه : (ا) قال رسول الله لعل الله ان الوضوء لا يجب الا على من نام مضطجعا فانه اذا اضطجع استرخت مفاصله ترندی شریف ، باب الوضوء من النوم، ص ۲۰، نمبر۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گہری نیند سونے سے وضوٹوٹے
Translation: (150) [8] The sleeping person moves so that there is possibility of his anus shifting. Explanation: In the previous three issues, the principle is that if sleep is so deep that intellect is gone, wudu breaks; if sleep is light and intellect remains, wudu does not break. Because after intellect is gone, all limbs become relaxed, and a person does not know if wind has passed or not. Therefore, deep sleep is considered like passing wind in terms of nullifying wudu. In the next three issues, the sleep is not deep. In issue number 8, the person is nodding off but the anus has not left the ground; this indicates sleep is light, so wudu does not break. If it is certain that the anus has left the ground, then wudu breaks. Proof: (1) The Messenger of Allah said: 'Perhaps Allah... indeed wudu is only obligatory upon one who sleeps lying down, because when he lies down, his joints relax.' (Tirmidhi, Chapter on wudu from sleep, p. 20, no. 77) This hadith indicates that deep sleep (lying down) breaks wudu.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding sleep and its effect on wudu. The author explains that deep sleep (where intellect is lost and joints relax) nullifies wudu, because one cannot be sure if wind exited. Light sleep (even with movement) does not break wudu if the anus remains on the ground, meaning the person is not fully unconscious. The proof is a hadith stating that wudu is required for one who sleeps lying down (i.e., deep sleep). The Hanafi school considers that only deep sleep, where one is unaware, nullifies wudu; light sleep does not.

Key Terms
معقل (ma'qil): Intellect; mental faculty that controls awareness.
مقعد (maq'ad): The anus; the seat that comes into contact with the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Does wudu break if a person is sitting and dozes off while nodding his head, but his anus remains on the ground?
A) Yes, because he is asleep.
B) No, because the anus is still on the ground and sleep is light.
C) Yes, because nodding off is deep sleep.
D) No, but only if he is sitting upright.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that only deep sleep (lying down with relaxed joints and loss of intellect) nullifies wudu; light sleep, indicated by the anus remaining on the ground, does not.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Actions That Do Not Break Wudu: Vomiting and Sleep
Listing five rulings on things that do not invalidate wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which types of vomiting and sleep break wudu according to the Hanafi school, and apply the principle of loss of senses to determine wudu validity.

Core Idea
Wudu breaks only with deep sleep (loss of senses) or vomiting a mouthful of impure food; light sleep and phlegm do not nullify.

In this lesson, we explore five scenarios where wudu remains intact even though some might think it breaks. The Hanafi school uses precise criteria: for vomiting, the amount and type; for sleep, the depth and posture. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly maintaining wudu in daily life and worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five actions listed
Read the Arabic/Urdu text and note the five items: (148) vomiting less than a mouthful, (149) vomiting phlegm even if abundant, (150) swaying sleep with possible anal departure, (151) seated sleep with buttocks fixed even if leaning, (152) prayer sleep in any posture.
The author groups these under 'what does not break wudu'.
2
Understand the condition for vomiting
Vomiting food breaks wudu only if it fills the mouth (because it contains stomach impurity). Vomiting phlegm does not break regardless of quantity, as phlegm originates from head/throat without impurity.
The proof is an athar from Hammad and a companion statement.
3
Analyze the sleep rulings
The key principle: wudu breaks only when deep sleep causes loss of senses ('aql) and relaxation of limbs. Light sleep, even with nodding, does not break as long as the buttocks remain firmly on the ground.
The hadith 'wudu is only obligatory on one who sleeps lying down' supports this.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on leaning sleep
Abu Hanifa holds that leaning sleep with buttocks fixed does not break wudu even if the support is removed. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it breaks. The author favors Abu Hanifa's view as the apparent madhhab.
The dispute hinges on whether the relaxation of limbs is certain.
5
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Given the rule 'wudu breaks with loss of senses', test cases like falling asleep at a desk (if buttocks are on chair, wudu remains; if lying down, it breaks).
Also apply to vomiting: a small burp of food does not break, but a full mouth of vomit does.

ترجمه : (١٥٠) [٨] سونے والا اتنا ہلنے لگا کہ اس کی مقعد زائل ہونے کا احتمال ہو۔ تشریح : آگے کے تینوں مسئلوں میں اصول یہ ہے کہ اتنی گہری نیند ہو کہ معقل زائل ہوگئی ہو تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا، اور ہلکی نیند ہو کہ ابھی عقل زائل نہیں ہوئی ہے تو اس سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ کیونکہ معقل زائل ہونے کے بعد ہی تمام اعضاء ڈھیلے ہو جاتے ہیں، اور آدمی کو پتہ نہیں چلتا کہ ہوا نکلتی ہے یا نہیں اس لئے گہری نیند کے سونے کو ہی ہوا نکلنے کے درجے میں رکھ کر وضو ٹوٹنے کا حکم لگا دیا گیا ہے ۔ آگے کے تینوں مسئلوں میں ابھی گہری نیند نہیں ہے اسی لئے مسئلہ نمبر ٨ میں ہے کہ جھونکا کھانے لگا ہے لیکن مقعد زمین سے نہیں اٹھی یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ ابھی نیند ہلکی ہے، اس لئے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ اگر اس بات کا یقین ہو جائے کہ مقعد زمین سے اٹھ چکی ہے تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
وجه : (ا) قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم انما الوضوء الا يجب الا على من نام مضطجعا فانه اذا اضطجع استرخت مفاصله (ترمذی شریف ، باب الوضوء من النوم، ص ٢٠، نمبر٧٧) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گہری نیند سونے سے وضو ٹوٹے گا۔ ہلکی نیند ہوتو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ (٢) اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس قال كان اصحاب رسول الله ينتظرون العشاء الآخرة حتى تخفق رءوسهم ثم يصلون ولا يتوضأون - (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الوضوء من النوم ص ٣٩ نمبر ٢٠٠ / ترمذی شریف ، باب الوضوء من النوم ص ٢١ نمبر ٧٨) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صحابہ نیند سے اتنے جھونکے کھاتے کہ سر ہلنے لگتے پھر بھی وضو نہیں کرتے ۔ کیونکہ ابھی مقعد زمین سے نہیں اٹھی۔
ترجمه : (١٥١) [٩] اور زمین پر مقعد کو ٹھیرا کرسونا، چاہے کسی چیز پر ٹیک لگا کر اس طرح سویا ہو کہ اگر اس کو ہٹادیا جائے تو آدمی گر جائے۔ دونوں مسئلوں میں ظاہر مذہب یہی ہے ۔
تشریح : آدمی کسی چیز پر اس طرح ٹیک لگا کر سویا ہے کہ اگر اس کو ہٹا دیا جائے تو آدمی گر جائے گا لیکن پھر بھی نیند اتنی ہی آئی ہے کہ ابھی تک مقعد زمین سے نکلی ہوئی ہے وہاں سے اٹھی نہیں ہے، اس لئے ظاہر مذہب یہی ہے کہ وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا، کیونکہ مقعد زمین سے ٹکی ہوئی ہے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ابھی تک نیند گہری نہیں ہے، جس سے تمام اعضاء ڈھیلے ہو جائیں ۔
ترجمه : (١٥٢) [١٠] اور نمازی کا سونا، چاہے رکوع یا سجدے کی حالت میں سنت کے موافق ہو۔ واللہ الموفق ۔
تشریح : نمازی رکوع سجدے، قیام، اور تشہد کی حالت میں سنت کے موافق سورہا ہے تو وہ ابھی زمین پر نہیں گرا ہے، جس کا مطلب ہے کہ اعضاء ابھی ڈھیلے نہیں ہوئے ہیں اس لئے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
وجه : (١) عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يسجد و ينام و ينفخ ثم يقوم فيصلى ولا يتوضأ ،فقلت له صليت و لم تتوضأ وقد نمت ؟ فقال : انما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعاً . زاد عثمان و هناد. فانه اذا اضطجع استرخت مفاصله (ابوداؤد ، باب فی الوضوء من النوم ص ١٣٩، نمبر ٢٠٢) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور سجدے کی حالت میں سوتے لیکن وضو نہیں کرتے کیونکہ گہری نیند نہیں تھی۔
اصول : زوال عقل سے وضو ٹوٹتا ہے۔ ورنہ نہیں۔
لغت : مقعد : قعد سے مشتق ہے، جس پر بیٹھتے ہیں، مراد ہے سرین۔ متمکن جمکن سے مشتق ہے، زمین پر ٹکا ہوا۔ مستندا: سند سے مشتق ہے، ٹیک لگایا ہوا۔ مصل: نماز پڑھنے والا ۔ علی السنۃ : سنت کے طریقے پر۔
Chapter: What does not break wudu. (148) Vomiting that does not fill the mouth. (149) Vomiting phlegm, even if much. (150) A sleeping person swaying such that there is a possibility of his anus leaving (its place). (151) Sleeping with buttocks firmly on the ground, even if leaning on something such that if it were removed he would fall - the apparent (position) in both. (152) A praying person sleeping, even if in ruku or sujud in accordance with the Sunnah. And Allah is the granter of success. Translation: (148) [6] And vomiting less than a mouthful. Explanation: If it fills the mouth, it has passed that wudu breaks; if it does not fill the mouth, wudu does not break. Proof: From Hammad regarding vomit: if it is little, there is no wudu; if it is much, then wudu (is required). (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah... etc.) This effect also shows that if vomit is less than a mouthful, wudu does not break. Translation: (149) [7] And vomiting of phlegm, even if abundant. Explanation: Vomiting food if it fills the mouth breaks wudu, but vomiting phlegm even if it fills the mouth does not break wudu. Proof: (1) Food contains impurity from the stomach, but phlegm is slimy and usually in the head or throat where there is no impurity, so vomiting phlegm even if full mouth does not break wudu because there is no impurity. (2) There is proof in this statement of a companion: I said to Ata... he said: By my life! I expectorate many things, then something comes from my throat and head; there is no wudu in that except what comes out of your stomach from your belly. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq...) This shows that if it is phlegm, there is no wudu. Translation: (150) [8] A sleeping person moves so much that there is a possibility of his anus leaving (the ground). Explanation: In the next three issues, the principle is that if sleep is deep such that sense (control) is lost, wudu breaks; if sleep is light such that sense is not lost, wudu does not break. Because after sense is lost, all limbs relax, and a person does not know if wind escapes or not, therefore deep sleep is treated as if wind escapes and wudu is ruled to break. In the next three issues, there is not yet deep sleep; therefore in issue #8, it says he is nodding but his buttocks have not left the ground; this indicates sleep is light, so wudu does not break. If it becomes certain that the buttocks have left the ground, then wudu breaks. Proof: (1) The Messenger of Allah said: 'Wudu is only obligatory on one who sleeps lying down, for when he lies down, his joints relax.' (Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that deep sleep breaks wudu; light sleep does not. (2) Another proof: from Anas: The companions of the Messenger of Allah would wait for isha prayer until their heads nodded, then they would pray and not perform wudu. (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that the companions would nod so much that their heads moved, yet they would not perform wudu, because their buttocks had not left the ground. Translation: (151) [9] And sleeping with the buttocks firmly on the ground, even if leaning on something in such a way that if it were removed he would fall. The apparent madhhab is that in both issues. Explanation: A person sleeps leaning on something so that if removed he would fall, but even then his sleep is such that his buttocks are still firmly on the ground and have not left it; therefore the apparent madhhab is that wudu does not break, because the buttocks are fixed to the ground, meaning sleep is not deep enough to relax all limbs. Translation: (152) [10] And a praying person sleeping, even in the state of ruku or sujud, as long as it is in accordance with the sunnah. And Allah is the granter of success. Explanation: A praying person sleeps in ruku, sujud, standing, or tashahhud in accordance with the sunnah; he has not fallen to the ground, meaning his limbs have not relaxed, so wudu does not break. Proof: (1) From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet would prostrate and sleep and snore, then stand and pray without performing wudu. I said: You prayed without wudu, and you had slept? He said: 'Wudu is only required on one who sleeps lying down.' Uthman and Hammad added: 'For when he lies down, his joints relax.' (Abu Dawood) This hadith shows that the Prophet would sleep in prostration but not perform wudu because the sleep was not deep. Principle: Wudu breaks with loss of senses; otherwise not. Vocabulary: Maq'ad: derived from qa'ada, the place one sits on, meaning buttocks. Mutamakkin: derived from tamakkana, fixed on the ground. Mustanidan: derived from sanad, leaning. Musallin: one who prays. 'Ali al-sunnah: in the manner of the sunnah.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from a Hanafi fiqh manual detailing actions that do NOT break wudu. The author lists five cases: (148) vomiting less than a mouthful, (149) vomiting phlegm even if abundant, (150) light sleep where the buttocks may not have left the ground, (151) sleeping upright with buttocks firmly seated, and (152) a praying person sleeping in a valid posture. The key principle underlying the sleep rulings is that wudu breaks only when sense ('aql) is lost due to deep sleep, causing all limbs to relax. The proof for this is the hadith that wudu is obligatory only on one who sleeps lying down because his joints relax. The author provides proofs for each: for vomiting, an athar from Hammad; for phlegm, a statement from a companion; for sleep, hadiths from Tirmidhi, Abu Dawood, etc. The commentary explains that vomiting food full mouth breaks wudu due to stomach impurity, but phlegm lacks that impurity. For sleep, as long as the buttocks are on the ground, sleep is considered light and wudu remains intact. The Hanafi position is clear: not all sleep breaks wudu; only deep sleep that removes control. This differs from some other schools that consider any sleep a wudu-breaker. The teacher should emphasize that the ruling is based on the principle of loss of senses, not just sleep itself.

Key Terms
مقعد (maq'ad): Buttocks, the part of the body on which one sits.
متمكن (mutamakkin): Firmly seated, with the buttocks fixed on the ground.
مستندا (mustanidan): Leaning on something (e.g., a support) while sleeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following does NOT break wudu?
A) Vomiting a mouthful of food
B) Vomiting phlegm even if a mouthful
C) Deep sleep lying down
D) Vomiting less than a mouthful of food

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wudu breaks only by deep sleep (loss of senses) or vomiting a mouthful of food; light sleep and phlegm do not nullify.

Taharah — Purification

Sleep That Does Not Break Wudu (Hanafi Rulings)
Ruling on sleep's effect on wudu with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sleep not breaking wudu and identify the key evidence from the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Wudu is not broken by light sleep where the buttocks remain fixed; only deep sleep lying down nullifies it.

One of the most common practical questions in taharah is whether sleep nullifies wudu. The Hanafi school makes a careful distinction: wudu is only broken when sleep causes the joints to relax, which typically occurs when one lies down. This lesson examines the ruling with its textual evidence, showing how the school distinguishes between light and deep sleep.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on when sleep does NOT break wudu. The act is sleep, and the ruling is that wudu remains valid under specific conditions (firm seating, prayer postures).
The ruling is a non-nullification (wudu remains).
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: the hadith of Anas about the Sahaba nodding off, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet slept in prostration and said wudu is only required for one who sleeps lying down.
Both are ahad hadith, so zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the hadith of Ibn Abbas, the operative phrase is 'innama al-wudu ala man nama mudtaji'an' – wudu is only for one who sleeps lying down. The attached reason: 'because when one lies down, his joints relax.' This indicates that sleep without joint relaxation does not break wudu.
The Hanafis take this as specifying the cause of nullification.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not accept this distinction and hold that any sleep breaks wudu. The difference stems from how they interpret the hadith and the general principle of loss of consciousness.
The Shafi'i view is based on other hadith and qiyas.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The author states 'ala al-zahir fihima' – the apparent madhhab is this. This is the mufta bihi position, relying on the explicit hadith of Ibn Abbas and the practice of the Sahaba.
Later Hanafi works (e.g., Hidayah) confirm this as the relied-upon view.

Chapter on what does not break wudu: His seat (buttocks planted) and sleep while seated firmly, even if leaning on something that if removed he would fall, according to the apparent ruling in both cases. And the sleep of a praying person, even if in ruku or sujud according to the sunnah manner. And Allah grants success. (Urdu: Light sleep does not break wudu. Its proof is the hadith of Anas: The companions of the Messenger of Allah would wait for the Isha prayer until their heads nodded, then they would pray and not perform wudu. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates that the companions would nod from sleep but did not perform wudu because their buttocks had not left the ground. Translation: (151) [9] Sleeping with buttocks firmly on the ground, even if leaning on something such that if removed he would fall. In both cases, the apparent madhhab is this. Explanation: A person leaned on something and slept such that if removed he would fall, but the sleep was such that his buttocks had not left the ground, so the apparent madhhab is that wudu is not broken because the buttocks are still on the ground, meaning the sleep is not deep enough to relax all limbs. Translation: (152) [10] And the sleep of a praying person, even if in ruku or sujud, according to the sunnah manner. And Allah grants success. Explanation: A praying person sleeps in ruku, sujud, qiyam, or tashahhud in the sunnah manner and has not fallen to the ground, meaning his limbs have not relaxed, so wudu is not broken. Proof: (1) From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet would prostrate and sleep and snore, then stand and pray without performing wudu. I said to him: You prayed without wudu and you slept? He said: Wudu is only required for one who sleeps lying down. Uthman and Hannad added: For when he lies down, his joints relax. (Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu from sleep, no. 202) This hadith indicates that the Prophet slept in prostration but did not perform wudu because the sleep was not deep. Principle: Wudu is broken by loss of consciousness, otherwise not. Vocabulary: Maq'ad: derived from qa'ada, meaning the place one sits on, i.e., buttocks. Mutamakkin: derived from tamakkun, fixed on the ground. Mustanidan: derived from sanad, leaning. Musallin: one who prays. Jami'at al-sunnah: in the manner of the sunnah.)
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on sleep and its effect on wudu in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating the matn: wudu is not broken if a person sleeps with their buttocks firmly planted on the ground, even if they are leaning on something that would cause them to fall if removed. Similarly, if a praying person sleeps in any posture of prayer (standing, bowing, prostrating, or sitting for tashahhud) in accordance with the sunnah, their wudu remains valid. The commentary then expands with Urdu explanation, emphasizing that the key is whether the sleep is deep enough to relax the limbs. The hadith of Anas shows that the companions would nod off while waiting for Isha but would not repeat wudu because their seat was still fixed. The hadith of Ibn Abbas directly proves that the Prophet slept in prostration without renewing wudu, and he clarified that wudu is only required for one who sleeps lying down, as that relaxes the joints. The principle derived is that wudu is nullified by loss of consciousness (zawal al-'aql), not by light sleep. The vocabulary section defines key terms like maq'ad (buttocks) and mutamakkin (fixed).

Key Terms
مقعد (maq'ad): The place one sits on, specifically the buttocks that are in contact with the ground.
نوم متمکن (nawm mutamakkin): Sleep while one's buttocks are firmly planted on the ground, without the body being completely relaxed.
مستندا (mustanidan): Leaning on something for support while sleeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the key factor that determines whether sleep breaks wudu?
A) The duration of sleep
B) Whether the sleeper is lying down and his joints relax
C) Whether the sleeper is in a state of janabah
D) The position of the head

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wudu is not broken by sleep unless it is deep enough to relax the joints, which typically occurs when lying down.

The First Cause of Ghusl: Semen Emission with Conditions
Lists causes and details first cause with conditions and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven causes of ghusl in the Hanafi school and apply the three conditions for the first cause to determine when ghusl is obligatory.

Core Idea
Ghusl is obligatory upon semen emission only if it reaches the exterior, is accompanied by desire, and is not from intercourse (which itself obligates ghusl).

The Hanafi school identifies seven causes that make ghusl obligatory. This lesson examines the first cause—semen emission—with its three key conditions. Understanding these conditions is essential for determining when one must perform ghusl, especially in cases of wet dreams or illness. The proofs from Quran and Sunnah establish the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Ghusl becomes fard (obligatory) upon occurrence of any of the seven listed causes. The first cause is the exit of semen (maniyy) with specific conditions.
The seven causes include: 1) semen emission, 2) insertion of the glans, 3) intercourse with corpse/animal with emission, 4) thin fluid after sleep, 5) moisture after unconsciousness, 6) menstruation, 7) postpartum bleeding.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 5:6: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves.' The word 'fathharu' is an imperative indicating obligation. A secondary proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah where the Prophet (s) said 'Yes, when she sees water (semen)' regarding a woman's wet dream.
The hadith confirms that ghusl is required for women upon semen emission, just as for men.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse commands purification when in janabah. Janabah is defined as the state requiring ghusl, which occurs upon semen emission or intercourse. The imperative indicates that ghusl is obligatory (fard). The hadith clarifies that emission itself is the trigger.
The authority of the Quran is qat'i in transmission (thubut), but the dalalah (indication) is zanni because the specific conditions are derived through interpretation.
4
Note the three conditions for the first cause
The passage specifies three conditions: (1) semen must exit to the apparent body (reaching the exterior), (2) it must be without intercourse (because intercourse itself obligates ghusl even without emission), and (3) the emission must be accompanied by sexual desire at the moment of separation from its place.
If any condition is missing, ghusl is not obligatory. For example, if semen is felt moving inside but does not exit, or if it exits due to illness without desire, ghusl is not required.
5
Apply to scenarios
Consider a wet dream: if semen exits, ghusl is obligatory; if no semen exits, it is not. If a person has intercourse without emission, ghusl is obligatory due to insertion of the glans. If semen exits from illness without desire, ghusl is not obligatory.
These distinctions are crucial for correct practice.

Ghusl becomes obligatory due to any of seven things: exit of semen without intercourse with desire from its place to the apparent body. ... Insertion of the glans (or its equivalent for the amputated) into one of the two passages (front or back) of a living person. Intercourse with a corpse or animal with emission. Finding a thin fluid after sleep if the organ was not erect before sleep. ... Presence of moisture after waking from intoxication or unconsciousness when it is predominantly thought to be semen. Explanation: There are three restrictions: [1] That the semen reaches the apparent body. If it is felt with desire but does not exit, ghusl is not obligatory. For example, in a wet dream, if semen exits, ghusl is obligatory; if not, it is not. [2] The second restriction is 'without intercourse' because if intercourse occurs, even without emission, ghusl is obligatory according to the Hanafis. [3] The third restriction is that desire was present at the time of separation from its place; thus if semen exits due to illness without desire, ghusl is not obligatory. Proof: (1) 'And if you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves' (Quran 5:6). This verse indicates that when in janabah, purify yourself i.e., perform ghusl. (2) For women, if semen exits, ghusl is obligatory. For this, the hadith of Umm Salamah: ... Is ghusl required for a woman if she has a wet dream? The Messenger of Allah said: Yes, when she sees water (i.e., semen). (Muslim, chapter...)
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the causes of ghusl (major ritual bath). The author first lists the seven causes that make ghusl obligatory: (1) exit of semen with desire, (2) insertion of the glans into the front or back passage of a living person (even without emission), (3) intercourse with a corpse or animal with emission, (4) finding a thin fluid after sleep if the organ was not erect, (5) moisture after unconsciousness/intoxication when predominantly thought to be semen, (6) menstruation, (7) postpartum bleeding. Additionally, washing the deceased is fard kifayah. The commentary then focuses on the first cause, explaining three conditions: semen must exit the body, it must be without intercourse (because intercourse itself obligates ghusl even without emission), and it must be accompanied by desire. The proofs are the Quranic verse (5:6) commanding purification after janabah, and the hadith of Umm Salamah confirming ghusl for women upon seeing semen.

Key Terms
مني (maniyy): Semen, the fluid that exits with sexual desire and necessitates ghusl.
جناية (janabah): The state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, caused by semen emission or intercourse.
حشفہ (hashafah): The glans of the penis; its insertion into the front or back passage of a living person necessitates ghusl even without emission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following scenarios does NOT require ghusl?
A) Ejaculation after a wet dream where semen reaches the external body
B) Intercourse with a living person without emission
C) Semen exiting due to illness without sexual desire
D) Finding a thin fluid after sleep if the organ was erect before sleep

Key Takeaway
Ghusl due to semen emission requires three conditions: exit to exterior, desire, and not from intercourse (which independently obligates ghusl).

Semen Emission: Conditions and Proofs for Obligatory Ghusl
States the first cause of obligatory ghusl with conditions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which semen emission makes ghusl obligatory and apply them to various scenarios.

Core Idea
Ghusl is obligatory only when semen exits the body with desire, not due to illness or without reaching the exterior.

In this lesson, we examine the first of the seven causes that obligate ghusl according to the Hanafi school: the emission of semen. The passage from Thamaratun Najah details three precise conditions and provides scriptural proofs. Mastering these conditions will help you distinguish when ghusl is truly required from when it is not, a common source of confusion in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine that the act in question is the emission of semen (maniy) and that the ruling is fard 'ayn (obligatory ghusl) when the conditions are met.
The passage lists seven causes; this is the first.
2
List the Three Conditions
Extract the three conditions: (1) semen must reach the exterior of the body, (2) emission must occur without intercourse, (3) emission must be accompanied by desire (shahwah) at the moment of separation from its source.
Each condition is derived from the Urdu commentary.
3
Examine the Proofs (Dalil)
Review the Quranic verse (5:6) and the hadith of Ali (radiyallahu anhu) that distinguish madhy from maniy. Understand how the imperative 'fa-tahharu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The 'hazaf' (forceful discharge) is a key marker of desired semen.
4
Distinguish from Similar Fluids
Note that madhy (pre-seminal fluid) and wady (post-urine discharge) do not require ghusl, and that thin, pleasureless discharge due to illness also does not obligate ghusl.
These distinctions are critical for correct fiqh application.
5
Apply to Scenarios
Test the conditions on hypothetical cases, such as a wet dream where semen is felt but does not exit, or emission due to illness without desire.
The passage provides two examples: wet dream with/without external emission.

Source Text
