فصل : (ما يوجب الاغتسال) يفترض الغسل بواحد من سبعة أشياء. (١٥٣) خروج المني إلى ظاهر الجسد إذا انفصل عن مقره بشهوة من غير جماع. (١٥٤) وتواري حشفة وقدرها من مقطوعها في أحد سبلي آدمي حي. ترجمه: (١٥٣) سات اشیاء میں سے کسی ایک چیز سے غسل فرض ہوتا ہے: [1] ظاہری جسم تک منی کا نکلنا جبکہ بغیر جماع کے شہوت کے ساتھ اپنی ٹھہرنے کی جگہ سے جدا ہوئی ہو۔ تشریح: یہاں تین قیدیں ہیں [1] ایک تو یہ کہ ظاہری جسم تک منی آئی ہو۔ منی شہوت کے ساتھ نکلتی ہوئی محسوس ہوئی لیکن ظاہری جسم تک نہیں آئی تو غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسے احتلام میں منی باہر آئی ہو تو غسل واجب ہوگا، اور منی باہر نہیں آئی ہو تو غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ [۲] دوسری قید بغیر جماع کی ہے، اس لئے کہ جماع کیا ہو تو منی نہ بھی نکلے تب بھی حنفیہ کے یہاں غسل واجب ہے۔ [۳] تیسری قید ہے کہ منی کی ٹھہرنے کی جگہ سے جدا ہوتے وقت شہوت ہوئی ہو، اس لئے اگر کسی بیماری کی وجہ سے منی نکلی، اور جگہ سے جدا ہوتے وقت شہوت نہیں ہوئی تو غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه: (١) وان كنتم جنبا فاطهروا ( آیت ٦، سورة المائدة (٥) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جنابت ہو تو طہارت حاصل کرو یعنی غسل کرو۔ (٢) عورت کو بھی منی نکلی ہو تو اس پر غسل واجب ہوگا، اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن أم سلمة ... فهل على المرأة من غسل إذا احتلمت؟ فقال رسول الله نعم إذا رأت الماء (یعنی المنی). (مسلم شریف، باب) (٣) شہوت کے ساتھ منی نکلی ہو تب واجب ہو گا اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علي رضي الله عنه قال له رسول الله عليه السلام لا تفعل إذا رأيت المذي فاغسل ذكرك وتوضأ وضوءك للصلاة فإذا فضحت الماء فاغتسل. (ابو داود شریف، باب فی المذي ص ١٣١، نمبر (٢٠٦) (٤) مسند احمد میں یوں عبارت ہے۔ إذا حذفت فاغتسل من الجنابة وإذا لم تكن حاذفا فلا تغتسل (مسند احمد علي بن أبي طالب، ج أول ص ١٧٣ نمبر ٨٤٩) حذفت اور فضحت کا ترجمہ ہے کہ منی کو دھکر نکلے تو غسل کرو۔ اور یہ شہوت کے ساتھ نکلنے میں ہوتا ہے (٥) مذي اور ودي بھی منی کا ایک حصہ ہے لیکن کو دکر نہیں نکلتی اس لئے ان میں غسل لازم نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح منی بیماری کی وجہ سے پانی کی طرح پتلی ہو جائے اور نکلتے وقت نہ لذت ہو اور نہ کودنا ہو اور ودي کی طرح نکلے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں منی کی خصوصیت نہ رہی اس لئے اس سے غسل واجب نہ ہوگا۔ (6) منی باہر آئے تب غسل فرض ہو گا، اندر رہے تو غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا، اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ قلت لعطاء: الرجل يحتلم فيدرك ذكره قبل أن تخرج النطفة، فيقبض عليه فيرجع هل عليه غسل؟ قال إن لم يخرج منه شيء فلا غسل عليه۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، ج أول ص ١٩٧، نمبر٩٧٧) اس قول تابعي میں ہے کہ منی نہ نکلے تو غسل واجب نہیں۔ لغت: مقره: قر سے مشتق ہے منی ٹھہرنے کی جگہ۔ ترجمه: (١٥٤) [٢] زندہ آدمی کے پیشاب یا پیخانہ کے راستے میں حشفہ چھپ جائے، اور جس کا حشفہ کٹ گیا ہو تو اس کی مقدار چھپ جائے تو غسل واجب ہوگا۔ تشریح: زندہ آدمی کے پیخانہ یا شرمگاہ میں مرد کا حشفہ چھپ جائے، اور اگر اس آدمی کا حشفہ کٹا ہوا ہو تو حشفہ کی مقدار ذکر اندر گھس جائے تو چاہے منی کا انزال نہ ہوا ہو تب بھی حنفیہ کے نزدیک غسل فرض ہے۔ پیخانہ کے راستے میں چاروں طرف رگوں کی رنگ ہوتی ہے، اس رنگ کے اندر پوری سپاری چھپ جائے تو غسل واجب ہوگا۔ اسی طرح عورت کی شرمگاہ میں جہاں عورت کا ختنہ کیا جاتا ہے وہاں رگوں کی رنگ ہوتی ہے اس رنگ کے اندر سپاری چھپ جائے تو غسل فرض ہو گا چاہے انزال نہ ہوا ہو یہاں تین قیدیں ہیں [1] زندہ آدمی کے پیخانہ کے راستے میں یا عورت کی شرمگاہ میں حشفہ گھس کر چھپ جائے تب غسل واجب ہوگا، اس لئے اگر مردہ آدمی کے پیخانہ یا پیشاب کے راستے میں حشفہ گھس جائے تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا۔ [٢] پیخانہ اور پیشاب کے راستے میں گھسے تو فرض ہوگا، کسی اور مقام میں گھسے تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہو گا [٣] پورا حشفہ گھسے، پس اگر پورا حشفہ نہ گھسا ہو تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا۔
Section: What necessitates ghusl. Ghusl is obligatory by one of seven things: (153) Emission of semen to the exterior of the body when it separates from its place of rest with desire without intercourse. (154) And concealment of the glans and its equivalent from the one whose glans is amputated in one of the two passages of a living human. Translation: (153) Ghusl becomes obligatory by one of seven things: [1] The exit of semen to the exterior of the body while it separates with desire from its place of rest without intercourse. Commentary: There are three conditions: [1] That the semen reaches the exterior. If semen is felt coming out with desire but does not reach the exterior, ghusl is not obligatory. For example, in a wet dream, if semen comes out, ghusl is obligatory; if it does not come out, ghusl is not obligatory. [2] The second condition is 'without intercourse' because if intercourse occurs, even if no semen is emitted, ghusl is obligatory according to the Hanafis. [3] The third condition is that at the time of separation from its place of rest, there is desire. So if semen is emitted due to illness without desire at separation, ghusl is not obligatory. Proofs: (1) 'And if you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves' (Quran 5:6) – this verse means that if you have janabah, perform purification i.e. ghusl. (2) Also for a woman, if semen is emitted, ghusl is obligatory. The hadith from Umm Salamah: 'Is there ghusl upon a woman when she has a wet dream?' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Yes, when she sees water (i.e. semen).' (Sahih Muslim) (3) The hadith from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not do so; if you see madhy, wash your penis and perform wudu like wudu for prayer, and if you discharge water (semen), then perform ghusl.' (Sunan Abi Dawud) (4) In Musnad Ahmad: 'If you discharge (with force), perform ghusl from janabah; and if you do not discharge (with force), do not perform ghusl.' (5) Madhy and wady are also parts of semen but do not exit with force, so ghusl is not required for them. Similarly, if semen becomes thin like water due to illness and exits without pleasure and force, it loses the characteristic of semen, so ghusl is not obligatory. (6) The statement of Ata: 'I asked Ata: A man has a wet dream and his penis touches before the semen exits, and he squeezes it and it goes back; is ghusl obligatory upon him?' He said: 'If nothing exits from him, there is no ghusl upon him.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Lexicon: 'Maqarra' is derived from 'qarr' meaning the place of rest. Translation: (154) [2] The glans becomes concealed in the two passages of a living human, and for the one whose glans is amputated, its equivalent becomes concealed, then ghusl becomes obligatory. Commentary: If the male glans enters and becomes concealed in the rectum or vulva of a living person, and if the person's glans is amputated, the equivalent length enters, then ghusl is obligatory even without emission according to the Hanafis. In the rectum, there is a ring of veins; if the entire glans is concealed inside this ring, ghusl becomes obligatory. Similarly, in the female vulva, the place of circumcision has a ring of veins; if the glans is concealed inside this ring, ghusl is obligatory even without emission. There are three conditions: [1] The glans enters and becomes concealed in the rectum or vulva of a living person. So if the glans enters the rectum or vulva of a dead person, ghusl is not obligatory without emission. [2] Entering the rectum or vulva makes ghusl obligatory; if it enters any other place, ghusl is not obligatory without emission. [3] The entire glans enters; if the entire glans does not enter, ghusl is not obligatory without emission.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah, a Hanafi fiqh work, is a detailed exposition of the first two of the seven causes that make ghusl obligatory. It begins by presenting the Arabic matn (core text) stating that ghusl becomes obligatory due to (1) emission of semen (mani) to the exterior of the body, provided it separates from its source (maqarr) with desire (shahwah) and without intercourse, and (2) concealment of the glans (hashafah) in either of the two passages of a living human. The Urdu commentary then elaborates on each. For the first cause, three conditions are listed: the semen must actually exit the body (if felt inside but not emitted, no ghusl), the emission must be without intercourse (since intercourse alone obligates ghusl per Hanafis even without emission), and the emission must be accompanied by desire (illness-induced emission without desire does not obligate ghusl). The commentary provides proofs: Quran 5:6 (command to purify from janabah), hadith from Umm Salamah (ghusl for women if they see semen in a wet dream), hadith from Ali (distinction between madhy and ghusl-requiring discharge), and the concept of 'hazaf' (forceful discharge). It also clarifies that madhy (pre-seminal fluid) and wady (post-urine discharge) do not require ghusl, and that thin, pleasureless discharge also does not. For the second cause, it explains that if the glans (or its equivalent in case of amputation) is fully concealed in the rectum or vulva of a living person, ghusl becomes obligatory even without ejaculation. This is based on the principle that the mere meeting of the circumcised parts (al-khitan) triggers janabah. Three conditions are given: the person must be alive, the concealment must be in the two passages (not elsewhere), and the entire glans must be concealed. If any condition is missing, ghusl is not obligatory without emission. This passage is a clear statement of the Hanafi position on these two major causes of ritual impurity requiring full-body washing.

Key Terms
منی (maniyy): Semen; the fluid emitted from the private parts that necessitates ghusl when it exits with desire and reaches the exterior.
مقر (maqarr): The place of rest or origin of semen; separation from this place with desire is a condition for ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for semen emission to make ghusl obligatory according to the Hanafi school?
A) The semen must reach the exterior of the body.
B) The emission must be accompanied by desire at separation from the source.
C) The emission must be from a living person.
D) The emission must be without intercourse.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl becomes obligatory due to semen emission only when three conditions are met: external exit, desire, and absence of intercourse.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Glans Concealment: A Cause of Ghusl Without Ejaculation
States the second cause of obligatory ghusl with conditions and inter-school difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which concealment of the glans obligates ghusl and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Maliki school.

Core Idea
Mere concealment of the glans in a living person's front or rear passage makes ghusl obligatory, even without ejaculation.

The second cause of obligatory ghusl is unique: it does not require any fluid emission. Instead, the simple act of fully concealing the glans (or its equivalent) in the two passages of a living person triggers janabah. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and differs from the Maliki view. In this lesson, we unpack the conditions and the evidence behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Recognize that the act is the concealment of the glans (hashafah) in one of the two passages (rectum or vulva) of a living human. The ruling is fard 'ayn (obligatory ghusl).
This applies equally to males and females, though the glans is male; for the female, the equivalent area is considered.
2
List the Three Conditions
Extract the conditions: (1) the person is alive, (2) the glans is fully concealed in either the front (vulva) or rear (rectum) passage, (3) the entire glans must be concealed (not partial).
The passage also mentions that if the glans is amputated, the equivalent length must be concealed.
3
Understand the Anatomical Boundary
The commentary describes a 'ring of veins' in both passages; the glans must be fully inside this ring for ghusl to be obligatory.
This anatomical detail helps in applying the rule to real situations.
4
Distinguish from Intercourse with a Dead Person
The passage specifically exempts concealment in a dead person's passages; without emission, no ghusl is required.
This is because the condition 'living' is explicitly mentioned.
5
Note the Inter-School Difference (Maliki)
The Hanafi school differs from the Maliki school: Hanafis say ghusl is obligatory with mere penetration, while Malikis require ejaculation for ghusl.
The Shafi'i school agrees with the Hanafi position on this issue.

(١٥٤) وتواري حشفة وقدرها من مقطوعها في أحد سبلي آدمي حي. ترجمه: (١٥٣) سات اشیاء میں سے کسی ایک چیز سے غسل فرض ہوتا ہے: [1] ظاہری جسم تک منی کا نکلنا جبکہ بغیر جماع کے شہوت کے ساتھ اپنی ٹھہرنے کی جگہ سے جدا ہوئی ہو۔ تشریح: یہاں تین قیدیں ہیں [1] ایک تو یہ کہ ظاہری جسم تک منی آئی ہو۔ منی شہوت کے ساتھ نکلتی ہوئی محسوس ہوئی لیکن ظاہری جسم تک نہیں آئی تو غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسے احتلام میں منی باہر آئی ہو تو غسل واجب ہوگا، اور منی باہر نہیں آئی ہو تو غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ [۲] دوسری قید بغیر جماع کی ہے، اس لئے کہ جماع کیا ہو تو منی نہ بھی نکلے تب بھی حنفیہ کے یہاں غسل واجب ہے۔ [۳] تیسری قید ہے کہ منی کی ٹھہرنے کی جگہ سے جدا ہوتے وقت شہوت ہوئی ہو، اس لئے اگر کسی بیماری کی وجہ سے منی نکلی، اور جگہ سے جدا ہوتے وقت شہوت نہیں ہوئی تو غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه: (١) وان كنتم جنبا فاطهروا ( آیت ٦، سورة المائدة (٥) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جنابت ہو تو طہارت حاصل کرو یعنی غسل کرو۔ (٢) عورت کو بھی منی نکلی ہو تو اس پر غسل واجب ہوگا، اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن أم سلمة ... فهل على المرأة من غسل إذا احتلمت؟ فقال رسول الله نعم إذا رأت الماء (یعنی المنی). (مسلم شریف، باب) (٣) شہوت کے ساتھ منی نکلی ہو تب واجب ہو گا اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علي رضي الله عنه قال له رسول الله عليه السلام لا تفعل إذا رأيت المذي فاغسل ذكرك وتوضأ وضوءك للصلاة فإذا فضحت الماء فاغتسل. (ابو داود شریف، باب فی المذي ص ١٣١، نمبر (٢٠٦) (٤) مسند احمد میں یوں عبارت ہے۔ إذا حذفت فاغتسل من الجنابة وإذا لم تكن حاذفا فلا تغتسل (مسند احمد علي بن أبي طالب، ج أول ص ١٧٣ نمبر ٨٤٩) حذفت اور فضحت کا ترجمہ ہے کہ منی کو دھکر نکلے تو غسل کرو۔ اور یہ شہوت کے ساتھ نکلنے میں ہوتا ہے (٥) مذي اور ودي بھی منی کا ایک حصہ ہے لیکن کو دکر نہیں نکلتی اس لئے ان میں غسل لازم نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح منی بیماری کی وجہ سے پانی کی طرح پتلی ہو جائے اور نکلتے وقت نہ لذت ہو اور نہ کودنا ہو اور ودي کی طرح نکلے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں منی کی خصوصیت نہ رہی اس لئے اس سے غسل واجب نہ ہوگا۔ (6) منی باہر آئے تب غسل فرض ہو گا، اندر رہے تو غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا، اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ قلت لعطاء: الرجل يحتلم فيدرك ذكره قبل أن تخرج النطفة، فيقبض عليه فيرجع هل عليه غسل؟ قال إن لم يخرج منه شيء فلا غسل عليه۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، ج أول ص ١٩٧، نمبر٩٧٧) اس قول تابعي میں ہے کہ منی نہ نکلے تو غسل واجب نہیں۔ لغت: مقره: قر سے مشتق ہے منی ٹھہرنے کی جگہ۔ ترجمه: (١٥٤) [٢] زندہ آدمی کے پیشاب یا پیخانہ کے راستے میں حشفہ چھپ جائے، اور جس کا حشفہ کٹ گیا ہو تو اس کی مقدار چھپ جائے تو غسل واجب ہوگا۔ تشریح: زندہ آدمی کے پیخانہ یا شرمگاہ میں مرد کا حشفہ چھپ جائے، اور اگر اس آدمی کا حشفہ کٹا ہوا ہو تو حشفہ کی مقدار ذکر اندر گھس جائے تو چاہے منی کا انزال نہ ہوا ہو تب بھی حنفیہ کے نزدیک غسل فرض ہے۔ پیخانہ کے راستے میں چاروں طرف رگوں کی رنگ ہوتی ہے، اس رنگ کے اندر پوری سپاری چھپ جائے تو غسل واجب ہوگا۔ اسی طرح عورت کی شرمگاہ میں جہاں عورت کا ختنہ کیا جاتا ہے وہاں رگوں کی رنگ ہوتی ہے اس رنگ کے اندر سپاری چھپ جائے تو غسل فرض ہو گا چاہے انزال نہ ہوا ہو یہاں تین قیدیں ہیں [1] زندہ آدمی کے پیخانہ کے راستے میں یا عورت کی شرمگاہ میں حشفہ گھس کر چھپ جائے تب غسل واجب ہوگا، اس لئے اگر مردہ آدمی کے پیخانہ یا پیشاب کے راستے میں حشفہ گھس جائے تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا۔ [٢] پیخانہ اور پیشاب کے راستے میں گھسے تو فرض ہوگا، کسی اور مقام میں گھسے تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہو گا [٣] پورا حشفہ گھسے، پس اگر پورا حشفہ نہ گھسا ہو تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا۔
Section: What necessitates ghusl. Ghusl is obligatory by one of seven things: (153) Emission of semen to the exterior of the body when it separates from its place of rest with desire without intercourse. (154) And concealment of the glans and its equivalent from the one whose glans is amputated in one of the two passages of a living human. Translation: (153) Ghusl becomes obligatory by one of seven things: [1] The exit of semen to the exterior of the body while it separates with desire from its place of rest without intercourse. Commentary: There are three conditions: [1] That the semen reaches the exterior. If semen is felt coming out with desire but does not reach the exterior, ghusl is not obligatory. For example, in a wet dream, if semen comes out, ghusl is obligatory; if it does not come out, ghusl is not obligatory. [2] The second condition is 'without intercourse' because if intercourse occurs, even if no semen is emitted, ghusl is obligatory according to the Hanafis. [3] The third condition is that at the time of separation from its place of rest, there is desire. So if semen is emitted due to illness without desire at separation, ghusl is not obligatory. Proofs: (1) 'And if you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves' (Quran 5:6) – this verse means that if you have janabah, perform purification i.e. ghusl. (2) Also for a woman, if semen is emitted, ghusl is obligatory. The hadith from Umm Salamah: 'Is there ghusl upon a woman when she has a wet dream?' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Yes, when she sees water (i.e. semen).' (Sahih Muslim) (3) The hadith from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not do so; if you see madhy, wash your penis and perform wudu like wudu for prayer, and if you discharge water (semen), then perform ghusl.' (Sunan Abi Dawud) (4) In Musnad Ahmad: 'If you discharge (with force), perform ghusl from janabah; and if you do not discharge (with force), do not perform ghusl.' (5) Madhy and wady are also parts of semen but do not exit with force, so ghusl is not required for them. Similarly, if semen becomes thin like water due to illness and exits without pleasure and force, it loses the characteristic of semen, so ghusl is not obligatory. (6) The statement of Ata: 'I asked Ata: A man has a wet dream and his penis touches before the semen exits, and he squeezes it and it goes back; is ghusl obligatory upon him?' He said: 'If nothing exits from him, there is no ghusl upon him.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Lexicon: 'Maqarra' is derived from 'qarr' meaning the place of rest. Translation: (154) [2] The glans becomes concealed in the two passages of a living human, and for the one whose glans is amputated, its equivalent becomes concealed, then ghusl becomes obligatory. Commentary: If the male glans enters and becomes concealed in the rectum or vulva of a living person, and if the person's glans is amputated, the equivalent length enters, then ghusl is obligatory even without emission according to the Hanafis. In the rectum, there is a ring of veins; if the entire glans is concealed inside this ring, ghusl becomes obligatory. Similarly, in the female vulva, the place of circumcision has a ring of veins; if the glans is concealed inside this ring, ghusl is obligatory even without emission. There are three conditions: [1] The glans enters and becomes concealed in the rectum or vulva of a living person. So if the glans enters the rectum or vulva of a dead person, ghusl is not obligatory without emission. [2] Entering the rectum or vulva makes ghusl obligatory; if it enters any other place, ghusl is not obligatory without emission. [3] The entire glans enters; if the entire glans does not enter, ghusl is not obligatory without emission.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah, a Hanafi fiqh work, is a detailed exposition of the first two of the seven causes that make ghusl obligatory. It begins by presenting the Arabic matn (core text) stating that ghusl becomes obligatory due to (1) emission of semen (mani) to the exterior of the body, provided it separates from its source (maqarr) with desire (shahwah) and without intercourse, and (2) concealment of the glans (hashafah) in either of the two passages of a living human. The Urdu commentary then elaborates on each. For the first cause, three conditions are listed: the semen must actually exit the body (if felt inside but not emitted, no ghusl), the emission must be without intercourse (since intercourse alone obligates ghusl per Hanafis even without emission), and the emission must be accompanied by desire (illness-induced emission without desire does not obligate ghusl). The commentary provides proofs: Quran 5:6 (command to purify from janabah), hadith from Umm Salamah (ghusl for women if they see semen in a wet dream), hadith from Ali (distinction between madhy and ghusl-requiring discharge), and the concept of 'hazaf' (forceful discharge). It also clarifies that madhy (pre-seminal fluid) and wady (post-urine discharge) do not require ghusl, and that thin, pleasureless discharge also does not. For the second cause, it explains that if the glans (or its equivalent in case of amputation) is fully concealed in the rectum or vulva of a living person, ghusl becomes obligatory even without ejaculation. This is based on the principle that the mere meeting of the circumcised parts (al-khitan) triggers janabah. Three conditions are given: the person must be alive, the concealment must be in the two passages (not elsewhere), and the entire glans must be concealed. If any condition is missing, ghusl is not obligatory without emission. This passage is a clear statement of the Hanafi position on these two major causes of ritual impurity requiring full-body washing.

Key Terms
حشفہ (hashafah): The glans of the penis; its concealment in the private parts of a living person necessitates ghusl even without ejaculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for ghusl due to glans concealment?
A) The person must be alive.
B) The glans must be partially concealed.
C) Ejaculation must occur.
D) The concealment must be in any orifice.

Key Takeaway
Full concealment of the glans in the front or rear passage of a living human makes ghusl obligatory, even without any emission.

Ghusl from Maniy: Conditions and Distinction from Madhi and Wadi
Ruling with proof on conditions for ghusl from maniy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which ghusl becomes wajib from maniy according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish maniy from madhi and wadi.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib only when maniy exits with desire and force; madhi and wadi require only wudu.

This passage explains the specific conditions that trigger the obligation of ghusl when maniy is emitted. Relying on hadith and the statements of early authorities, the Hanafi school distinguishes maniy from other fluids, establishing that not every discharge necessitates a full bath. Understanding these conditions helps avoid unnecessary acts of worship and ensures one's purification is correct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ghusl from maniy. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory), not fard. Wajib is a level of obligation below fard, based on ahad hadith.
Hanafi terminology distinguishes fard (qat'i proof) from wajib (zanni proof).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith narrated by 'Ali (ra): 'When you see madhi, wash your organ and perform wudu; when you expel water (maniy), perform ghusl.' This is found in Abu Dawud and Musnad Ahmad.
The hadith uses the imperative 'faghtasil' (perform ghusl).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) from the Prophet indicates obligation (wujub). Since this hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), the obligation is wajib, not fard.
If the proof were qat'i, the ruling would be fard.
4
Distinguish the types of fluids
The passage distinguishes maniy (requires ghusl) from madhi and wadi (require only wudu). The key differences are desire, force, and consistency.
Madhi exits with slight desire without force; wadi is thick, exits after urination or illness, without desire.
5
Identify exceptions
If maniy becomes thin due to illness and exits without pleasure and force, it is treated like wadi and does not require ghusl. Also, if maniy does not exit (e.g., caught after wet dream), ghusl is not required.
The athar from 'Ata' supports the condition of actual exit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ما يوجب الغسل مقره بشهوة من غير جماع (۱۵۴) وتوارى حشفة وقدرها من مقطوعها في احد سبيلى آدمى حيّ وجوب الغسل على المرأة بخروج المنى منها ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۷۱۲/۳۱۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت کو منی نکلی ہو تو غسل واجب ہے ولة ۔ (۳) شہوت کے ساتھ منی نکلی ہو تب واجب ہو گا اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علی رضی الله عنه قال له رسول الله عل الله لا تفعل اذا رأيت المذی فاغسل ذکرک و توضأ وضوئك للصلوة فاذا فضحت الماء فاغتسل . (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی المذی ص ۱۳۱، نمبر (۲۰۶) (۴) مسند احمد میں یوں عبارت ہے۔ اذا حذفت فاغتسل من الجنابة واذا لم تكن حاذفا فلا تغتسل (مسند احمد علی بن ابی طالب، ج اول ص ۱۷۳ نمبر ۸۴۹ ) حذفت اور فضحت کا ترجمہ ہے کہ منی کو دکر نکلے تو غسل کرو۔ اور یہ شہوت کے ساتھ نکلنے میں ہوتا ہے (۵) مذی اور ودی بھی منی کا ایک حصہ ہے لیکن کو دکر نہیں نکلتی اس لئے ان میں غسل لازم نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح منی بیماری کی وجہ سے پانی کی طرح پتلی ہو جائے اور نکلتے وقت نہ لذت ہواور نہ کودنا ہواورودی کی طرح نکلے تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں منی کی خصوصیت نہ رہی اس لئے اس سے غسل واجب نہ ہوگا۔ (1) منی باہر آئے تب غسل فرض ہو گا ، اندر ر ہے تو غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا، اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ قلت لعطاء : الرجل يحتلم فیدرک ذکره قبل ان تخرج النطفة ، فيقبض عليه فيرجع هل عليه غسل ؟ قال ان لم يخرج منه شيء فلا غسل علیہ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، ج اول ص ۱۹۷، نمبر۹۷۷ ) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ منی نہ نکلے تو غسل واجب نہیں۔
Chapter: What necessitates ghusl. (154) And the concealment of the glans and the measure of what remains of a circumcised person in one of the two passages of a living human, and the obligation of ghusl on a woman due to the exit of maniy from her. Page 145 number 712/313. In this hadith: If a woman's maniy exits, then ghusl is wajib. (3) If maniy exits with desire, then it becomes wajib. For this there is this hadith: 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) said to him: Do not do that. When you see madhi, wash your organ and perform wudu like for prayer, and when you expel water (maniy), then perform ghusl.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-madhi, p. 131, no. 206) (4) In Musnad Ahmad, the expression is: 'When you propel (maniy), then perform ghusl from janabah, and if you do not propel, then do not perform ghusl.' (Musnad Ahmad, 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, vol. 1, p. 173, no. 849) 'Hadafta' and 'fadahhta' mean: eject maniy with force, then perform ghusl. And this occurs when it exits with desire. (5) Madhi and wadi are also a part of maniy, but they do not exit with force, so ghusl is not necessary for them. Similarly, if maniy becomes thin like water due to illness and exits without pleasure and without force, and exits like wadi, then manifestly its quality of maniy is gone, so ghusl will not be wajib. (1) If maniy comes out, then ghusl becomes fard; if it remains inside, ghusl is not fard. For this, there is this athar: I said to 'Ata': A man has a wet dream and catches his organ before the drop exits, and he squeezes it so it goes back; is there ghusl upon him? He said: If nothing exits from him, then no ghusl upon him. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, vol. 1, p. 197, no. 977) In this saying of a Tabi'ee, it is stated that if maniy does not exit, ghusl is not wajib.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm bi dalil) regarding the conditions that necessitate ghusl from maniy. The author begins by stating the general rule: ghusl is wajib when maniy exits with desire (shahwah). This is based on the hadith narrated by Imam al-Bukhari and Muslim where the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) says: 'When you see madhi, wash your organ and perform wudu; when you expel water (maniy), perform ghusl.' The term 'fadahhta' or 'hadhafat' indicates maniy exiting with force, which is a sign of desire. The passage then distinguishes maniy from madhi and wadi. Madhi and wadi are parts of maniy but do not exit with force, so they do not necessitate ghusl; only wudu is required. Furthermore, if maniy becomes thin due to illness and exits without the typical characteristics of pleasure and force, it is not considered maniy for the purpose of ghusl. Finally, the author cites a famous narration from 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah: if a person has a wet dream but catches his organ before maniy exits and it recedes, ghusl is not required because the maniy did not exit.

Key Terms
منی (maniy): The fluid that exits with sexual desire and force, necessitating ghusl.
مذی (madhi): Pre-seminal fluid that exits without force, requiring only wudu.
ودی (wadi): Thick white fluid discharged after urination or due to illness, requiring wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following requires ghusl according to the Hanafi school?
A) Exiting of madhi
B) Exiting of wadi
C) Exiting of maniy with desire and force
D) Exiting of any fluid from the private parts

Key Takeaway
Ghusl from maniy is wajib only when the fluid exits with desire and force; otherwise, only wudu is needed.

The Obligation of Ghusl upon Concealment of the Glans
Ruling with proof on ghusl due to concealment of the glans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl when the glans is concealed, list the three conditions, and cite the primary hadith proof.

Core Idea
Ghusl becomes wajib when the glans is fully concealed in the front or back passage of a living person, even without emission.

This passage addresses the second cause of mandatory ghusl: the meeting of circumcised parts (iltaqa al-khitanan). The Hanafi school, based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him), holds that mere concealment of the glans in either the vagina or anus obligates ghusl. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its three conditions, and the textual proof, as well as the historical madhhab discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the concealment of the male glans (hashafah) in one of two passages (front or back) of a living person. The ruling is that ghusl becomes wajib, even without ejaculation.
The passage explicitly states that ghusl is fard, but in Hanafi usul, the binding level is wajib due to the zanni thubut of the hadith.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The main proof is the hadith: 'When he sits between her four limbs and the circumcised part touches the circumcised part, ghusl becomes obligatory.' This is a clear textual command.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is qati because the phrase 'wajaba al-ghusl' explicitly indicates obligation.
3
Understand the three conditions
The passage lists three conditions for ghusl to be wajib: (1) the person must be living, (2) the glans must be inserted into either the anus or the vagina (not other openings), (3) the entire glans must be concealed within the constriction (ring) of the passage.
If any condition is missing, ghusl is not required without emission.
4
Examine the madhhab dispute
Some early scholars held that emission is required for ghusl. The Hanafi response cites the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b showing that the initial permission was abrogated, and the final ruling is based on mere concealment.
The thamarah al-khilaf is largely theoretical: in practice, all schools require ghusl after full intercourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لغت : مقرة: قر سے مشتق ہے ہنی ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ۔ ترجمه : (۱۵۴) [۲] زندہ آدمی کے پیشاب یا پیخانہ کے راستے میں حشفہ چھپ جائے ، اور جسکا حشفہ کٹ گیا ہو تو اس کی مقدار چھپ جائے تو غسل واجب ہوگا ] تشریح : زندہ آدمی کے پیخانہ یا شرمگاہ میں مرد کا حشفہ چھپ جائے ، اور اگر اس آدمی کا حشفہ کٹا ہوا ہو تو حشفہ کی مقدار ذ کر اندر گھس جائے تو چاہے منی کا انزال نہ ہوا ہو تب بھی حنفیہ کے نزدیک غسل فرض ہے۔ پیخانہ کے راستے میں چاروں طرف رگوں کی رنگ ہوتی ہے، اس رنگ کے اندر پوری سپاری چھپ جائے تو غسل واجب ہوگا۔ اسی طرح عورت کی شرمگاہ میں جہاں عورت کا ختنہ کیا جاتا ہے وہاں رگوں کی رنگ ہوتی ہے اس رنگ کے اندر سپاری چھپ جائے تو غسل فرض ہو گا چاہے انزال نہ ہوا ہو یہاں تین قیدیں ہیں [1] زندہ آدمی کے پیخانہ کے راستے میں یا عورت کی شرمگاہ میں حشفہ گھس کر چھپ جائے تب غسل واجب ہوگا، اس لئے اگر مردہ آدمی کے پیخانہ یا پیشاب کے راستے میں حشفہ گھس جائے تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا ۔ [۲] پیخانہ اور پیشاب کے راستے میں گھسے تو فرض ہوگا، کسی اور مقام میں گھسے تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہو گا [۳] پورا حشفہ گھسے، پس اگر پورا حشفہ نہ گھسا ہو تو انزال کے بغیر غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا۔ (۱۵۵) وانزال المني بوطئ ميتة او بهيمة (۱۵۶) ووجود ماء رقيق بعد النوم اذا لم يكن ذكره وجه : (ا) عن عائشة قال رسول الله الا الله اذا جلس بين شعبها الاربع ومس الختان الختان فقد وجب الغسل . (مسلم شریف باب بیان ان الجماع الخ ص ۱۵۶ نمبر ۷۸۵/۳۴۹ ابوداؤد، باب فی الا کسال، ص ۴۱ نمبر ۲۱۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت کے ختنے کی جگہ مرد کے ختنے کی جگہ سے مل جائے ، یعنی سپاری چھپ جائے تو غسل فرض ہو جائے گا۔ چاہے انزال ہوا ہو یا نہ ہوا ہو۔ (۲) ان ابی بن کعب اخبره ان رسول الله الله انما جعل ذلك رخصة في اول الاسلام لقلة الثياب ثم امر بالغسل ونهى عن ذلك (ابو داؤد ، باب فی الا کسال، ص ۱۴۱، نمبر ۲۱۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف حشفہ غائب ہونے سے غسل واجب ہوگا چاہے انزال نہ ہوا ہو۔ (۳) دبر میں بھی لذت کامل ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس میں بھی حشفہ غائب ہونے پر غسل لازم ہوگا۔ اس حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله من وجدتموه يعمل عمل قوم لوط فاقتلوا الفاعل والمفعول به) - ابوداود شریف ، باب فیمن عمل عمل قوم لوط ص ۶۲۹ نمبر ۴۴۶۲) اس حدیث میں دبر میں کرنے والے کو بھی قتل کیا گیا جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اس سے بھی لذت کاملہ ہوتی ہے۔
Lexicology: 'Maqarrah' is derived from 'qarra' meaning place of settling. Translation of (154): [When the glans is concealed in the urinary or fecal passage of a living person, or when the measure of a circumcised person's glans is concealed, then ghusl becomes wajib.] Explanation: If a man's glans is concealed in the anus or vagina of a living person, or if that person's glans is circumcised, then the measure of the glans entering inside, even if no maniy is emitted, then according to the Hanafis, ghusl is fard. In the anal passage, there is a circular constriction (ring of muscles); when the entire glans is concealed within that constriction, ghusl becomes wajib. Similarly, in a woman's vagina where circumcision is done, there is a constriction; when the glans is concealed inside that constriction, ghusl becomes fard even if no emission occurs. There are three conditions: [1] The glans must be inserted and concealed in the anus of a living person or the woman's vagina; thus if it is inserted into the passage of a dead person, ghusl is not fard without emission. [2] It must be inserted into the anus or the front passage; if inserted into any other place, ghusl is not fard without emission. [3] The entire glans must be inserted; if the entire glans is not inserted, ghusl is not fard without emission. (155) And emission of maniy by intercourse with a dead female or an animal. (156) And finding thin fluid after sleep, when his organ was not erect. Proof: (a) From 'Aishah: The Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) said: 'When he sits between her four limbs and the circumcised part touches the circumcised part, then ghusl becomes obligatory.' (Muslim, Bab Bayan ..., p. 156, no. 785/349; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Iksal, p. 41, no. 216) In this hadith, when the place of circumcision of the woman touches that of the man, that is, the glans is concealed, then ghusl becomes fard, whether or not emission occurs. (2) Ubayy ibn Ka'b informed him that the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) made that a concession in early Islam due to scarcity of clothing, then he commanded ghusl and forbade that. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Iksal, p. 141, no. 214) From this hadith, it is understood that ghusl becomes wajib solely by the concealment of the glans, even if no emission occurs. (3) In the anus, there is also complete pleasure, so ghusl is necessary upon concealment of the glans there. There is an indication to this in the hadith: Ibn 'Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) said: 'Whoever you find doing the act of the people of Lut, kill the doer and the one to whom it is done.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi man 'amala 'amala qawm Lut, p. 629, no. 4462) In this hadith, the one doing it in the anus is also killed, which indicates that there is complete pleasure in it as well.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm bi dalil) detailing the second cause that necessitates ghusl: the meeting of the circumcised parts (iltaqa al-khitanan) or concealment of the glans (khafa' al-hashafah). The author begins by defining the term 'maqarrah' and then translates the matn. The key point is that when the male glans (hashafah) enters and is concealed in the front or back passage of a living person, ghusl becomes wajib, even without emission. This is based on the hadith: 'When he sits between her four limbs and the circumcised part touches the circumcised part, ghusl becomes obligatory.' This hadith is the primary dalil. The Hanafi position requires that the glans be fully concealed inside the constriction (ring) of the respective passage. Three conditions are given: (1) the person must be living; (2) it must be one of the two passages (front or back); (3) the entire glans must be inserted. The passage then cites additional proofs: the narration of Ubayy ibn Ka'b indicating that initial permission was abrogated, and the hadith about the people of Lut, which implies that anal intercourse also produces the full pleasure that necessitates ghusl.

Key Terms
حشفہ (hashafah): The glans of the penis, the area that is circumcised.
ختان (khitan): The place of circumcision; for men the glans, for women a part of the labia.
رگ (rag): In this context, the constriction or ring of muscle in the passages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for ghusl to be wajib upon concealment of the glans according to the Hanafi school?
A) The person must be dead.
B) The glans must be inserted into the anus or vagina of a living person.
C) Only emission of maniy.
D) The glans must be inserted into any body cavity.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl becomes wajib upon full concealment of the glans in the front or back passage of a living person, based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Ghusl Required After Intercourse with Dead or Animal Only if Emission Occurs
Ruling statement on ghusl obligation for dead/animal intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl after intercourse with a dead female or animal and apply the condition that triggers obligation.

Core Idea
Dead or animal feels no pleasure, so ghusl is wajib only upon emission.

The general rule for living partners is that ghusl becomes wajib as soon as the glans is concealed, regardless of emission, because both sides experience pleasure. This lesson covers an exception: when the partner is a dead female or an animal, there is no reciprocal pleasure, so the obligation of ghusl is postponed until actual emission of maniy occurs. Understanding this exception helps you avoid unnecessary ghusl and correctly identify when janabah applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is intercourse (wati') with a dead female (maytah) or a quadruped animal (bahimah). The ruling is that ghusl becomes wajib only if maniy is emitted; otherwise it is not wajib.
This is an exception to the general case with living partners.
2
Understand the underlying cause (illah)
The cause for ghusl from intercourse is either actual emission or the presumption of mutual pleasure. With a dead partner or animal, pleasure is absent on their side, so only emission (the presence of maniy) triggers janabah.
The Hanafi principle: 'ghusl from intercourse requires either emission or full pleasure (tamām al-ladhdha).'
3
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
If a man penetrates a deceased woman without any emission of maniy, ghusl is not wajib. If emission occurs, ghusl becomes wajib. The same applies to an animal.
Remember: the dead is a maytah (female human corpse), the animal is any quadruped.
4
Compare with the general rule for living partners
In living partners, concealment of the glans (ijtimā' al-khitānayn) alone makes ghusl wajib, because both parties are presumed to experience pleasure. For dead/animal, this presumption is absent, so emission is required.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵۵) وانزال المني بوطئ ميتة او بهيمة تشریح : میت کو یا چوپائے کو لذت نہیں ہے، اس لئے صرف ایک جانب لذت ہوئی اس لئے لذت کا ملہ نہیں ہوئی ،اس لئے انکے قبل یاد بر میں وطی کرنے سے جب تک انزال نہ ہو غسل واجب نہیں ہو گا۔
(155) And the emission of maniy by intercourse with a dead female or an animal. Explanation: A dead person or an animal does not experience pleasure. Therefore, only one side experienced pleasure; thus complete pleasure did not occur. Hence, when having intercourse with their front or back, ghusl is not wajib until emission occurs.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (hukm) that clarifies an exception to the general rule. The third cause requiring ghusl is the emission of maniy from intercourse with a dead female or an animal. Since the dead or animal does not experience pleasure, the 'full pleasure' criterion is not met; therefore, ghusl is not required upon mere concealment of the glans. It only becomes wajib if maniy is actually emitted. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that ghusl from intercourse requires either emission or full pleasure (which is presumed from living partners).

Key Terms
میته (maytah): A dead female human.
بھیمہ (bahimah): A quadruped animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only if maniy is emitted
C) Always, because it is still intercourse
D) Never, because the dead cannot cause janabah

Key Takeaway
Intercourse with a dead female or animal only triggers ghusl when maniy is emitted because the partner lacks pleasure.

Ghusl for Finding Thin Fluid After Sleep
Explaining that finding thin fluid after sleep requires ghusl if the organ was not erect before sleep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for finding thin fluid after sleep and apply the condition regarding prior erection to determine when ghusl is wajib.

Core Idea
Thin fluid after sleep without prior erection makes ghusl wajib, as it indicates a wet dream.

This passage addresses the fourth cause of ghusl in the Hanafi school: finding thin fluid (ma' raqiq) upon waking from sleep, which is presumed to be maniy from a wet dream. The key condition is whether the person had an erection before sleeping—if not, the fluid is likely maniy and ghusl becomes wajib. The proof is drawn from a narration of al-Hasan al-Basri regarding emission during intercourse, analogized to the sleep scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Finding thin fluid after sleep. What is the hukm? Ghusl becomes wajib.
The fluid is presumed to be maniy unless there is evidence to the contrary.
2
Note the condition and its rationale
The condition is that the organ was not erect before sleep. This distinguishes maniy from madhi (pre-seminal fluid), which often accompanies erection and does not require ghusl.
If there was an erection, the fluid could be madhi and only wudu is needed.
3
Analyze the proof cited
The text cites a narration from al-Hasan al-Basri: for intercourse outside the vagina, ghusl is only required if emission occurs. Similarly, finding fluid after sleep indicates emission, so ghusl is wajib.
This is a qawl Tabi'i, which is an accepted source of proof in the Hanafi school.
4
Consider the ikhtilaf
Some scholars require certainty that the fluid is maniy. The Hanafi school presumes it is maniy in the absence of an erection before sleep, based on the analogy to emission.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih; both views are legitimate.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
If a person wakes up with a thin damp spot and does not recall an erection, ghusl is wajib. If they recall an erection, they should perform wudu and wash the area.
In doubt, one should perform ghusl to be safe, as it covers both possibilities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵۶) ووجود ماء رقيق بعد النوم اذا لم يكن ذكره وجه : عن الحسن في الرجل يصيب من المرأة فى غير فرجها قال : ان هي انزلت اغتسلت و ان هي لم تنزل توضأت و غسلت ما اصاب من جسدها من ماء الرجل - (مصنف ابن ابي شبيبة ، ۱۰۹ فی الرجل يجامع امرأته دون الفرج ، ج اول ص ۸۹ نمبر ۹۹۲ / مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب الرجل يصيب امرأته فی غیر الفرج ، ج اول ص ۱۹۶، نمبر ۹۷۱) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ فرج کے علاوہ میں وطی کرے تو انزال ہوگا تو غسل واجب ہوگا اور انزال نہ ہو تو غسل واجب نہیں ہے ، اور یہاں فرج کے علاوہ میں وطی ہے اس لئے انزال کے بغیر غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔
(156) And the existence of thin water after sleep, when his organ was not erect. Proof: From al-Hasan concerning a man who has intercourse with a woman in other than her private part; he said: If she emits (maniy), she performs ghusl; if she does not emit, she performs wudu and washes off from her body any of the man's fluid that has gotten on her. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 109, vol. 1, p. 89, no. 992; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, vol. 1, p. 196, no. 971) In this saying of a Tabi'ee, it states that if one has intercourse other than in the private part and maniy is emitted, ghusl becomes wajib; if no emission, ghusl is not wajib. And here, it is intercourse other than in the private part, so without emission, ghusl is not wajib.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm bi dalil) regarding the fourth cause for ghusl: finding thin fluid (likely maniy) on the body or clothes after sleep if there was no erection before sleep. The text uses the Arabic 'wujid ma' raqiq' meaning if a person wakes up and finds thin fluid that is suspected to be maniy from a wet dream, and they did not have an erection before sleep, then ghusl is wajib. The proof cited is a narration from al-Hasan al-Basri regarding intercourse outside the vagina (interfemoral intercourse). In that case, ghusl is only required if maniy is emitted. Similarly, after sleep, the presence of such fluid indicates emission, so ghusl is necessary. The condition of no prior erection distinguishes the fluid from pre-seminal fluid (madhi) which would not require ghusl.

Key Terms
ماء رقيق (ma' raqiq): Thin fluid found after sleep, likely maniy from a wet dream.
انتشار ذکر (intishar dhikr): Erection of the male organ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If thin fluid is found and there was an erection before sleep
B) If thin fluid is found and there was no erection before sleep
C) If any moisture is found regardless of erection
D) Only if the fluid is definitely maniy

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, finding thin fluid after sleep without prior erection triggers the obligation of ghusl.

Ghusl from Intercourse with a Dead Person or Animal: Emission Required
States ruling and proof for ghusl from intercourse with dead or animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that ghusl from intercourse with a dead person or animal is wajib only upon emission, and apply the condition of emission to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Ghusl from intercourse with an insentient being requires emission, not mere penetration.

This passage clarifies a nuanced rule regarding ritual purity (ghusl) after intercourse with a corpse or animal. Unlike intercourse with a living spouse, where ghusl is obligatory regardless of emission, here the lack of mutual pleasure shifts the criterion to actual emission. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary ghusl and ensures correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being discussed? Intercourse (wat') with a corpse (mayyitah) or an animal (bahimah). The ruling: ghusl is wajib only if emission (inzal) occurs.
The passage lists this as one of the causes of ghusl.
2
Understand the rationale
Why is emission required here? The corpse or animal has no capacity for pleasure (lidhdhah), so 'complete pleasure' (al-lidhdhah al-kamilah) is not achieved for both parties. Thus, penetration alone does not trigger ghusl; emission becomes the decisive factor.
This rationale is explicitly given in the commentary.
3
Examine the proof
What evidence supports this ruling? The statement of al-Hasan al-Basri (a tabi'i) about a man having intercourse with a woman in other than her vagina: if she emits, she does ghusl; if not, she does wudu and washes any semen traces. This shows emission is the trigger when full mutual pleasure is absent.
4
Compare with normal intercourse
How does this differ from intercourse with a living spouse? In normal intercourse, ghusl is wajib with penetration regardless of emission because both parties can experience pleasure. The absence of one-sided pleasure changes the condition.
This contrast helps solidify the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ما يوجب الغسل (۱۵۵) وانزال المني بوطئ ميتة او بهيمة (۱۵۶) ووجود ماء رقيق بعد النوم اذا لم يكن ذكره منتشرا قبل النوم (۱۵۷) ووجود بلل ظنّه منيا بعد افاقته من سكر واغماء (۱۵۸) و بحيض ونفاس (۱۵۹) وغسل الميت فرض كفاية. تشريح: ميں تك ياه چوپائے كو لذت نہيں ہے، اس لئے صرف ايك جانب لذت ہوئي اس لئے لذت كاملہ نہيں ہوئي، اس لئے انكے قبل يادبر میں وطي كرنے سے جب تك انزال نہ ہو غسل واجب نہيں ہو گا۔ وجه: عن الحسن في الرجل يصيب من المرأة فى غير فرجها قال: ان هي انزلت اغتسلت و ان هي لم تنزل توضأت و غسلت ما اصاب من جسدها من ماء الرجل - (مصنف ابن ابي شبية، 109 فی الرجل يجامع امرأته دون الفرج، ج اول ص 89 نمبر 992 / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الرجل يصيب امرأته فی غیر الفرج، ج اول ص 196، نمبر 971)
Chapter on what makes ghusl obligatory. (155) Emission of semen by intercourse with a corpse or an animal. (156) Finding thin water after sleep if his penis was not erect before sleep. (157) Finding moisture he assumes to be semen after recovering from intoxication or unconsciousness. (158) And by menstruation and postpartum bleeding. (159) And washing the deceased is a communal obligation. Explanation: The corpse or animal has no pleasure, so only one side has pleasure, thus complete pleasure is not achieved. Therefore, from intercourse in their front or rear, ghusl is not obligatory until emission occurs. Proof: From al-Hasan regarding a man who has intercourse with a woman in other than her vagina: he said, 'If she has an orgasm, she performs ghusl; and if she does not have an orgasm, she performs wudu and washes from her body what touched her of the man's water.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 109; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, 971)
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage begins with a list of causes of ghusl, then focuses on ruling 155. The author explains that since a corpse or animal cannot feel pleasure, the condition of 'complete pleasure' (al-lidhdhah al-kamilah) is not met for both parties. Therefore, ghusl is not obligatory with penetration alone; it requires actual emission. The proof is the saying of al-Hasan al-Basri (a tabi'i) that in non-vaginal intercourse, ghusl is only required if there is emission. This is a clear statement that emission is the trigger in the absence of full mutual pleasure.

Key Terms
انزال (inzal): Emission of semen, which is the trigger for ghusl in certain cases of intercourse without full mutual pleasure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always obligatory
B) Only if there is emission
C) Only if penetration is in the front
D) Never obligatory

Key Takeaway
Ghusl from intercourse with an insentient being depends on emission, not penetration.

Ghusl for Finding Thin Fluid After Sleep: Between Certainty and Assumption
Ruling with proof for ghusl on thin fluid after sleep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for finding thin moisture after sleep, identify the conditions that determine whether ghusl is obligatory, and apply the hadith proof to distinguish between semen and madhy.

Core Idea
Ghusl after sleep is wajib only if the moisture is presumed semen and no prior erection existed.

A common confusion arises when a person wakes up to find moisture on their body or clothes. Is ghusl always required? The Hanafi school, drawing on a precise hadith, teaches that the ruling depends on the state before sleep and the strength of the assumption that the fluid is semen. This lesson unpacks the conditions and the proof, helping you apply the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
The act is finding thin moisture (balal) after sleep. The default is that if it is presumed to be semen, ghusl becomes wajib. But if it could be madhy (pre-ejaculate) due to prior erection, ghusl is not obligatory unless certainty exists.
The ruling is not absolute; it hinges on context.
2
Analyze the Key Condition: Erection Before Sleep
If the penis was not erect before sleep, the moisture is likely semen from a wet dream, so ghusl is wajib. If it was erect, the shrinking could release madhy, so ghusl is not wajib unless one is certain it is semen.
The presence of erection shifts the presumption toward madhy.
3
Apply the Concept of Ghālib al-Ẓann (Dominant Assumption)
In the Hanafi school, a dominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) suffices to obligate ghusl when no prior erection. But if erection existed, only certain knowledge (yaqīn) of semen obligates ghusl.
Certainty overrides doubt, but mere possibility does not.
4
Examine the Dalīl: The Hadīth of ʿĀʾishah
The Prophet ﷺ was asked about a man who finds moisture but does not remember a wet dream; he commanded ghusl. When asked about a man who dreams but finds no moisture, he said no ghusl. This distinguishes between actual emission and mere dream.
The hadith is the primary evidence; it does not mention prior erection, but Hanafi scholars derive the condition from complementary proofs.
5
Combine the Ruling with the Proof
The hadith orders ghusl for moisture without memory; Hanafis interpret 'moisture' as presumed semen. The condition of no erection before sleep is added because if erection existed, the moisture could be madhy, which does not require ghusl. Only certainty of semen overrides that.
Thus the ruling is: ghusl wajib if moisture found AND no prior erection AND ghalabat al-zann that it is semen; if prior erection, only certainty obligates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵۶) ووجود ماء رقيق بعد النوم اذا لم يكن ذكره منتشرا قبل النوم [ تو غسل واجب ہوگا ] تشریح: سونے کے بعد جسم یا بستر پر اس طرح کا پانی پایا گیا جس سے گمان غالب ہوتا ہے کہ یہ احتلام کی منی ہے تو غسل واجب ہوگا کیونکہ انزال ہو گیا، لیکن اگر سونے سے پہلے ذکر منتشر ہو تو اس بات کا احتمال ہے کہ ذکر سکڑنے کی وجہ سے ندی نکلی، اس لئے غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا، لیکن سونے سے پہلے ذکر کے منتشر ہونے کے باوجود یہ یقین ہو جائے کہ یہ منی کا پانی ہے تو غسل واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یقین سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ انزال ہوا ہے۔ وجه: عن عائشة قالت سئل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الرجل يجد البلل و لا يذكر احتلاما؟ قال: يغتسل، و عن الرجل يرى انه قد احتلم و لم يجد بللاً؟ قال لا غسل علیه (ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فيمن يستيقظ ویری بللا ولا یذکر احتلاما ص 30 نمبر 113 ابوداود شریف، باب فی الرجل یجد البلل فی منامه، ص 44، نمبر 236)
(156) And finding thin water after sleep if his penis was not erect before sleep [then ghusl is obligatory]. Explanation: After sleep, if such water is found on the body or bed that dominant assumption is that it is semen from a wet dream, then ghusl is obligatory because emission occurred. But if before sleep his penis was erect, there is a possibility that it is madhy (prostatic fluid) due to the penis shrinking, so ghusl is not obligatory. However, if despite the erection before sleep, one is certain it is semen water, then ghusl is obligatory because certainty shows emission occurred. Proof: From 'A'ishah who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about a man who finds moisture but does not remember a wet dream. He said: 'He performs ghusl.' And about a man who sees that he had a wet dream but does not find moisture. He said: 'No ghusl is due on him.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for finding a thin fluid after sleep. The key condition is the state of the penis before sleep. If it was not erect, the fluid is likely semen (maniy) from a wet dream, so ghusl is obligatory. If it was erect, the fluid could be madhy (pre-ejaculate) caused by the shrinking of the erection, so ghusl is not obligatory unless one is certain it is semen. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet distinguishes between finding moisture (requiring ghusl) and only dreaming without moisture (no ghusl). Certainty overrides doubt.

Key Terms
بلل (balal): Moisture found on body or clothes after sleep, interpreted as semen when dominant assumption supports it.
مدی (madhy): Prostatic fluid that can be emitted due to arousal or erection; does not require ghusl but requires wudu and washing the area.
غسل (ghusl): Ritual full-body washing required after sexual discharge (janābah).
احتلام (ihtilām): Wet dream, sexual emission during sleep.
یقین (yaqīn): Certainty, the highest level of conviction that overrides doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man finds moisture after sleep and his penis was erect before sleep, when does ghusl become obligatory?
A) Always
B) Never
C) Only if he is certain it is semen
D) Only if he remembers a wet dream

Key Takeaway
Ghusl after sleep is wajib only when the moisture is presumed to be semen and no prior erection existed, or when certainty of semen exists despite erection.

Ghusl upon Finding Moisture After Intoxication or Unconsciousness
States ruling for ghusl upon finding moisture after intoxication or unconsciousness using qiyas to sleep.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for ghusl after finding moisture from intoxication or unconsciousness and explain the qiyas to sleep with the 'illa of suspension of intellect.

Core Idea
Finding moisture with dominant assumption of semen after intoxication obligates ghusl – same as after sleep.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a person regains consciousness after intoxication or fainting and finds moisture, unsure if it is semen. The Hanafi school rules that ghusl is wajib if the dominant assumption (zann ghalib) indicates it is semen. The ruling is derived through qiyas (analogy) to sleep, because both involve suspension of intellect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is finding moisture after regaining consciousness from intoxication or unconsciousness. The ruling: ghusl is wajib if the dominant assumption is that it is semen.
2
Identify the proof
The proof is qiyas to sleep. For sleep, the ruling is known from hadith: if one wakes and finds moisture with dominant assumption of semen, ghusl is wajib.
The exact hadith is from 'A'ishah (ra) but not quoted here.
3
Extract the 'illa
The effective cause ('illa) is the suspension of intellect (dhahab al-'aql), which makes the person unaware of emission, so the same ruling applies.
4
Apply the qiyas
Since intoxication and unconsciousness share the same 'illa as sleep (suspension of intellect), the ruling from sleep is transferred to these states.
5
Note the condition
The condition is dominant assumption (zann ghalib), not certainty. This is a Hanafi facilitation in matters of purity.
If there is no dominant assumption, ghusl is not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵۷) [۵] نشہ اور بے ہوشی سے ہوش میں آنے کے بعد تری موجود ہونا جب اس کے منی ہونے کا ظن غالب ہو۔ تشریح: نشہ اور بیہوشی نیند کی طرح ہے، کیونکہ ان میں بھی عقل معطل ہوتی ہے، اس لئے نشہ سے یا بیہوشی سے ہوش میں آنے کے بعد جسم یا کپڑے پر تری دیکھی اور گمان غالب ہے کہ یہ منی نکلی ہے تو اس سے غسل واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ آدمی جنبی ہوگیا۔
(157) [5] Existence of moisture after regaining consciousness from intoxication and unconsciousness, when the dominant assumption is that it is semen. Explanation: Intoxication and unconsciousness are like sleep, because in them too, the intellect is suspended. Therefore, after regaining consciousness from intoxication or unconsciousness, if one sees moisture on the body or clothes and the dominant assumption is that this is emitted semen, then ghusl is obligatory because the person has become junub.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage equates intoxication and unconsciousness to sleep in terms of the intellect being inactive. Therefore, the same ruling applies: if upon regaining consciousness one finds moisture with a strong assumption it is semen, ghusl becomes wajib. This is based on qiyas (analogy) to the ruling for sleep, since the 'illa (effective cause) is the suspension of intellect and the possibility of emission without awareness.

Key Terms
ظن غالب (zann ghalib): Dominant assumption (over 50% certainty) that the moisture is semen, sufficient to obligate ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for ghusl to be wajib when moisture is found after intoxication?
A) Certainty that it is semen
B) Dominant assumption that it is semen
C) Memory of a wet dream
D) Whether one had sexual thoughts

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling uses qiyas to sleep to obligate ghusl upon finding moisture with dominant assumption of semen after intoxication or unconsciousness, due to suspension of intellect.

Obligation of Ghusl After Menstruation and Postpartum Bleeding
States ruling that ghusl after hayd and nifas is obligatory even if occurred before Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl after hayd and nifas and apply it when the bleeding occurred before embracing Islam.

Core Idea
Ghusl after menstruation is wajib even if it occurred before Islam — the cause is established, and Islam does not erase physical obligations.

This lesson addresses a subtle but important ruling: a woman who experienced menstruation or postpartum bleeding before embracing Islam must still perform ghusl after becoming Muslim. The source clarifies that the cause (sabab) for ghusl existed, and embracing Islam does not eliminate the physical obligation. The proofs are drawn from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its General Ruling
The passage states that after menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas) cease, ghusl is obligatory (wajib).
This is the default ruling for all Muslim women.
2
Recognize the Special Case – Before Islam
The passage then specifies that this ruling applies even if the bleeding occurred before the woman embraced Islam, provided she never performed ghusl after it ended.
The key phrase: 'if these matters occurred before embracing Islam then also ghusl is obligatory'.
3
Understand the Underlying Principle – Sabab (Cause)
The obligation remains because the cause (sabab) for ghusl – the cessation of menstrual or postpartum bleeding – existed. Embracing Islam does not retroactively erase a physical cause that already triggered an obligation.
This is a fiqh principle: obligations linked to a cause are not waived by a change in status.
4
Review the Proofs (Dalil)
The author cites Quran 2:222 (command to approach after purification) and hadiths on ghusl from menstruation. These proofs show that ghusl is a condition for resumed relations and worship.
The dalil block in the toolbox provides further detail on the proof structure.
5
Apply to a Concrete Scenario
Consider a woman who had three menstrual cycles before becoming Muslim. She must now perform three ghusls (one for each cycle) because the cause existed for each. The ruling is not retroactively waived.
The practical application shows the ruling's scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵۸) [6] حیض اور نفاس کے بعد، اور صحیح روایت یہ ہے کہ یہ چیزیں اسلام لانے سے پہلے حاصل ہوئی ہو [ تب بھی غسل لازم ہوگا ] تشریح: حیض اور نفاس ختم ہونے کے بعد غسل لازم ہوگا۔ اگر حیض اور نفاس اسلام لانے سے پہلے آئے ہوں اور ابھی غسل بھی نہیں کیا ہے کہ مسلمان ہوگئی تب بھی غسل لازم ہوگا، کیونکہ غسل کا سبب پایا گیا۔ وجه: (1) یسئلونک عن المحيض قل هو اذى فاعتزلوا النساء في المحيض ولا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن فاذا تطهرن فاتوهن من حيث امركم الله (آیت 222، سورۃ البقرۃ) (2) عن عائشة ان امرأة سألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن غسلها من المحيض؟ فامرها كيف تغتسل قال خذى فرصة من مسك فتطهري بها الخ (بخاری، مسلم) (3) عن معاذ عن النبي قال اذا مضى للنفساء سبع ثم رأت الطهر فلتغتسل ولتصل (مستدرک حاکم، بیہقی)
(158) [6] After menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and the sound narration is that these matters occurred before embracing Islam [then also ghusl is obligatory]. Explanation: After the cessation of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, ghusl is obligatory. If menstruation and postpartum bleeding occurred before embracing Islam and she has not yet performed ghusl when she became Muslim, then also ghusl is obligatory because the cause for ghusl occurred. Proofs: (1) Quran 2:222: 'They ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they are purified. And when they have purified themselves, then come to them from where Allah has ordained for you.' (2) Hadith from 'A'ishah about a woman asking the Prophet about ghusl from menstruation. (3) Hadith from Mu'adh that a postpartum woman after seven days should perform ghusl and pray.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage covers the obligation of ghusl after menstruation and postpartum bleeding ceases. Importantly, it addresses a subtle issue: if the bleeding occurred before a woman embraced Islam and she never performed ghusl for it, she must still do so after becoming Muslim because the cause (sabab) existed. The proofs are from the Quran (2:222) indicating purification after menstruation, and from Sunnah (hadith of 'A'ishah and Mu'adh) commanding ghusl for hayd and nifas.

Key Terms
حیض (hayd): Menstrual bleeding that obligates ghusl after its cessation.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding that obligates ghusl after its cessation.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers a legal obligation; here, the cessation of bleeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a woman who experienced postpartum bleeding before embracing Islam and never performed ghusl?
A) She must perform ghusl after embracing Islam because the cause existed.
B) She is not required to perform ghusl because Islam wipes away past obligations.
C) She must perform ghusl only if she remembers the exact date of the bleeding.
D) The ruling depends on whether she had menstruated before that.

Key Takeaway
The cause for ghusl (cessation of hayd or nifas) is a physical event that creates an obligation, and embracing Islam does not erase that obligation.

Ghusl for the Deceased is a Communal Obligation
States the ruling of ghusl al-mayyit as fard kifayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that washing the deceased is fard kifayah and explain the communal vs. individual obligation distinction.

Core Idea
Washing the deceased is a communal duty; if some do it, all are absolved.

This lesson establishes a fundamental ruling in funeral rites: washing the deceased is not a personal duty on every Muslim, but a collective one. Understanding this distinction ensures the community acts responsibly without unnecessary burden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The act is 'ghusl al-mayyit' (washing the deceased). Determine its hukm (legal ruling) as stated: fard kifayah.
Fard kifayah means a collective obligation, distinct from fard 'ayn.
2
Understand the scope of fard kifayah
If some members of the community perform the washing, the obligation is lifted from all. If nobody performs it, the entire community becomes sinful.
This incentivizes communal responsibility.
3
Recognize the absence of conditions in the text
The concise text does not list conditions (e.g., the deceased must be Muslim). The ruling itself is unconditional in this statement.
Full conditions are known from other sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵۹) وغسل الميت فرض كفاية.
(159) And washing the deceased is a communal obligation.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This is a concise ruling that ghusl for the deceased is fard kifayah (communal obligation). If some Muslims perform it, the obligation is lifted from the rest. The text does not provide proofs here, but it is established from the Sunnah (e.g., the Prophet's command to wash his daughter Zainab).

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A collective obligation; if fulfilled by some Muslims, the rest are absolved; if neglected, all are sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if no one washes a deceased Muslim?
A) The deceased remains impure
B) The obligation is automatically waived
C) All Muslims become sinful
D) The family is solely responsible

Key Takeaway
Washing the deceased is a communal obligation (fard kifayah); the community must ensure it is performed.

Causes Requiring Ghusl and the Principle of Certainty
Rulings and proofs for obligatory ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that necessitate ghusl in the Hanafi school and apply the principle of certainty to determine when ghusl is required.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib only upon certainty of mani emission or after menstruation/lochia; doubt does not obligate.

This passage from the chapter on ghusl (taharah) lists the specific events that make ghusl obligatory. The Hanafi school emphasizes the role of certainty (yaqin) in establishing the need for ghusl. We will examine the primary causes—emission of mani, recovery from intoxication or unconsciousness with dominant presumption, and the end of menstruation and lochia—and the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah that supports them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts that necessitate ghusl
The text lists: emission of mani (with certainty), finding wetness after unconsciousness/intoxication (with dominant presumption), and menstruation/lochia.
2
Locate the proof for each cause
For mani, the hadith from Aisha; for menstruation/lochia, Quran 2:222 and hadith from Aisha and Mu'adh.
These appear in the lesson passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith links ghusl to certainty; the verse links purification to intercourse; each indicates obligation.
4
Note the condition of certainty vs. doubt
The hadith explicitly differentiates: if certain of mani, ghusl; if not, no ghusl.
This is a core Hanafi principle.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Practice with cases where certainty is absent or present.

Source Text
