فصل ما يوجب الغسل منتشرا قبل النوم (۱۵۷) ووجود بلل ظنّه منيا بعد افاقته من سكر واغماء (۱۵۸) و بحيض ونفاس لئے غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا، لیکن سونے سے پہلے ذکر کے منتشر ہونیکے باوجود یہ یقین ہو جائے کہ یہ منی کا پانی ہے تو غسل واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یقین سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ انزال ہوا ہے۔ وجه : . عن عائشة قالت سئل النبي علي الله عن الرجل يجد البلل و لا يذكر احتلاما ؟ قال : يغتسل ،و عن الرجل يرى انه قد احتلم و لم يجد بللاً ؟ قال لا غسل علیه ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فيمن يستيقظ ویری بللا ولا یذکر احتلاما ص ۳۰ نمبر ۱۱۳ ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الرجل یسجد البلته فی منامه، ص ۴۴، نمبر ۲۳۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ منی نکلنے کا یقین ہو تو غسل واجب ہوگا، اور شک ہو تو غسل فرض نہیں ہوگا۔ ترجمه : (۱۵۷) [۵] نشہ اور بے ہوشی سے ہوش میں آنے کے بعد تری موجود ہونا جب اس کے منی ہونے کا ظن غالب ہو۔ تشریح : نشہ اور بیہوشی نیند کی طرح ہے، کیونکہ ان میں بھی عقل ماؤف ہوتی ہے، اس لئے نشہ سے یا بیہوشی سے ہوش میں آنے کے بعد جسم یا کپڑے پر تری دیکھی اور گمان غالب ہے کہ یہ منی نکلی ہے تو اس سے غسل واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ آدمی جنبی ہوگیا۔ ترجمه : (۱۵۸) [1] حیض - 1- انفاس کے بعد، اور صحیح روایت یہ ہے کہ یہ چیزیں اسلام لانے سے پہلے حاصل ہوئی ہو [ تب بھی غسل لازم ہوگا ] تشریح : حیض اور نفاس ختم ہونے کے بعد فسل لازم ہوگا۔ اگر حیض، اور نفاس اسلام لانے سے پہلے آئے ہوں اور ابھی غسل بھی نہیں کیا ہے کہ مسلمان ہوگئی تب بھی غسل لازم ہوگا، کیونکہ فسل کا سبب پایا گیا۔ رض وجه : (۱) یسئلونک عن المحيض قل هو اذى فاعتزلوا النساء في المحيض ولا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن فاذا تطهرن فاتوهن من حيث امركم الله (آیت ۲۲۲ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) آیت میں اشارہ ہے کہ حائضہ غسل کرے تب جماع کرو۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة ان امرأة سألت النبي علي الله عن غسلها من المحيض؟ فامرها كيف تغتسل قال خذى فرصة من مسك فتطهري بها الخ ( بخاری شریف، باب دلك المرأة نفسها اذا تطهرت من الحيض، ص ۲۵، نمبر ۱۳۱۴ مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب استعمال المغتسلة من الحيض فرصة من مسك ،ص ۱۴۷، نمبر ۳۲۳۲/ ۷۳۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حائضہ پر غسل فرض ہے۔ (۳) عن معاذ عن النبي قال اذا مــضـى لـلـنفـساء سبع ثم رأت الطهر فلتغتسل ولتصل (مستدرک للحاکم ، کتاب الطہارة ، ج اول ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۶۲۶ سند للبیھقی ، باب النفاس ص ۵۰۵، نمبر ۱۶۱۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفساء بھی خون ختم ہونے کے بعد فسل کرے گی ۔ ترجمه : (۱۵۹) اور میت کو نسل دینا فرض کفایہ ہے۔ فصل ما لا يغتسل منها ولو حصلت الاشياء المذكورة قبل الاسلام فى الاصح (۱۵۹) ويفترض تغسيل الميت كفاية. فصل : (عشرة اشياء لا يغتسل منها تشریح : یہ غسل فرض کفایہ ہے یعنی کچھ لوگ غسل دے دے تو سب کی جانب سے ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ چونکہ فرض عین نہیں ہے اس لئے مصنف نے اس کو نہیں گنا۔ صلى الله وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ام عطية الانصارية قالت دخل علينا رسول الله له حين توفيت ابنته فقال اغسلنها ثلاثا او خمسا او اكثر من ذالك ان رأيتن ذالك بماء وسدر و اجعلن في الآخرة كافورا - ( بخاری شریف، باب غسل الميت و وضوه بالماء والسد ر ص ۲۰۱، نمبر ۱۲۵۳ر مسلم شریف ، باب فی غسل المیت ، ص ۱۳۷۷، نمبر ۲۱۶۸/۹۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ میت کو غسل دے، اور دوسری عورت نے غسل دیا تو حضور کی جانب سے ادا ہو گیا، یہ فرض کفایہ ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ فصل: دس چیزوں سے غسل نہیں کیا جا تا کہ ۱۰۔ چیزوں سے غسل واجب نہیں ہوتا، ایک نظر میں اندی۔ ....... ودی۔ .... احتلام بغیر تری کے۔ اور صحیح مذہب میں بچہ پیدا ہونا اس کے بعد بغیر خون دیکھے۔ اور ایسے کپڑے سے دخول کرنا جو وجودلذت سے مانع ہو۔ اور انگلی وغیرہ کا احد السبیلین میں داخل کرنا۔ چوپایہ۔ یا میت سے بلا انزال ولی کرنا۔ ...... باکرہ سے اس طرح بلا انزال جماع کرے کہ اس کی بکارت زائل نہ ہو۔ ☆☆☆
Chapter on what necessitates ghusl: (157) [Fluid] emitted before sleep? and (158) finding wetness thought to be mani after recovering from intoxication or unconsciousness. And due to menstruation and lochia, ghusl will not be obligatory, but if before sleep, despite emission of fluid, it becomes certain that it is mani water, then ghusl will be obligatory because it is known with certainty that emission occurred. Proof: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about a man who finds wetness but does not remember a wet dream? He said: He should perform ghusl. And about a man who sees that he had a wet dream but does not find wetness? He said: No ghusl upon him. (Tirmidhi, chapter on one who wakes up and finds wetness but does not remember a wet dream, p.30 no.113; Abu Dawud, chapter on a man who finds wetness in his sleep, p.44 no.236). This hadith indicates that if there is certainty of mani emission, ghusl is obligatory; if there is doubt, ghusl is not obligatory. Translation (157): [5] The presence of wetness after regaining consciousness from intoxication or unconsciousness, when it is the dominant presumption that it is mani. Explanation: Intoxication and unconsciousness are like sleep because in them the intellect is impaired. Therefore, after regaining consciousness from intoxication or unconsciousness, if one sees wetness on the body or clothes and the dominant presumption is that mani came out, then ghusl becomes obligatory because the person has become junub. Translation (158): [1] After menstruation and lochia, and the correct narration is that if these things occurred before embracing Islam, [even then ghusl is necessary]. Explanation: After menstruation and lochia end, ghusl becomes obligatory. If menstruation and lochia occurred before embracing Islam and one had not performed ghusl and then became Muslim, even then ghusl is obligatory because the cause of ghusl existed. Proof: (1) They ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they purify themselves. And when they have purified themselves, then come to them from where Allah has commanded you. (Quran 2:222) The verse indicates that a menstruating woman should perform ghusl before intercourse. (2) Hadith: From Aisha that a woman asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about her ghusl from menstruation? He ordered her how to perform ghusl. He said: Take a piece of musk and purify yourself with it, etc. (Bukhari, chapter on a woman rubbing herself when purifying from menstruation, p.25 no.1314; Muslim, chapter on the desirability of a woman bathing from menstruation using a piece of musk, p.147 no.3232/738). This hadith shows that ghusl is obligatory upon a menstruating woman. (3) From Mu'adh from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: When seven days have passed for the woman in lochia, then if she sees purity, let her perform ghusl and pray. (Mustadrak al-Hakim, book of purification, vol.1 p.284 no.626; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on lochia, p.505 no.1617). This hadith shows that a woman in lochia should also perform ghusl after the blood ends. Translation (159): And washing the deceased is a communal obligation. Chapter on things from which ghusl is not performed. And if the mentioned things occurred before Islam, according to the correct view (159), and it is obligatory to wash the deceased as a communal obligation. Chapter: Ten things from which ghusl is not performed. Explanation: This ghusl is a communal obligation, meaning if some people perform the ghusl, it suffices on behalf of all. And since it is not an individual obligation, the author did not count it. Proof: (1) In this hadith: From Umm Atiyya al-Ansariyya said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) entered upon us when his daughter died and said: Wash her three times, or five times, or more than that if you see fit, with water and sidr, and put camphor in the last. (Bukhari, chapter on washing the deceased and their ablution with water and sidr, p.201 no.1253; Muslim, chapter on washing the deceased, p.1377 no.2168/939). This hadith indicates that the deceased should be washed, and another woman washed her, and it sufficed on behalf of the Prophet; this is evidence that it is a communal obligation. Chapter: Ten things from which ghusl is not performed. Ten things from which ghusl is not obligatory, at a glance: Madhy, Wadi, wet dream without wetness, and according to the correct madhhab, birth of a child without seeing blood, and penetration with a cloth that prevents the sensation of pleasure, and insertion of a finger etc. into one of the two passages, an animal, or intercourse with a deceased without emission, ... intercourse with a virgin without emission such that her hymen is not removed. ☆☆☆
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section from the chapter on ghusl in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by stating the causes that necessitate ghusl: emission of mani (with certainty), finding wetness after unconsciousness/intoxication with dominant presumption, and after menstruation/lochia. He then provides a hadith from Aisha (RA) establishing that certainty of mani necessitates ghusl, while doubt does not. The commentary clarifies that the ruling applies whether the person was asleep, intoxicated, or unconscious, as the intellect is impaired in all these states. The Quranic verse (2:222) and additional hadith are cited to prove that ghusl is obligatory after menstruation and lochia. The passage then transitions to the ruling that washing the deceased is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), supported by the hadith of Umm Atiyya. Finally, the chapter lists ten things that do not necessitate ghusl, though the list is incomplete in the text. The author explains that since ghusl for the deceased is not an individual obligation, it was not counted among the obligatory ghusls earlier. The list includes madhy, wadi, wet dream without wetness, birth without blood, penetration with a barrier, insertion of finger, bestiality, intercourse with a dead body without emission, and intercourse with a virgin without breaking the hymen. These are all cases where ghusl is not wajib because there is no certainty or emission of mani.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the entire body with water reaching every part, performed to remove major ritual impurity (janabah).
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation; if some Muslims perform it, the obligation is lifted from all; if none perform, all are sinful.
مني (mani): Semen; its emission with lust and spurt necessitates ghusl upon certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on ghusl for a person who finds wetness on their clothes after waking up but is not certain it is mani?
A) Ghusl is wajib because wetness indicates impurity.
B) Ghusl is not wajib because there is doubt.
C) Ghusl is mustahab to be safe.
D) Ghusl is wajib only if one remembers having a wet dream.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires certainty of mani for ghusl to be wajib; doubt does not obligate.

beginner

Ghusl for the Deceased: Communal Obligation and Non-Required Situations
Rulings and proofs for ghusl of deceased and non-required cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why ghusl for the deceased is fard kifayah and identify the situations where ghusl is not required.

Core Idea
Washing the deceased is a communal obligation; ten specific situations do not necessitate ghusl.

This passage continues the chapter on ghusl by addressing the obligation of washing the deceased. It establishes that this ghusl is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) supported by the hadith of Umm Atiyya. The text then lists ten cases where ghusl is not required, such as madhy, wadi, and wet dream without wetness. We will examine these rulings and their basis.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for washing the deceased
The text says washing the deceased is a communal obligation (fard kifayah).
2
Identify the proof
The hadith of Umm Atiyya where the Prophet commanded washing his daughter, and it sufficed that some women did it.
This establishes that it is not an individual duty.
3
List the ten things that do not necessitate ghusl
The text mentions examples: madhy, wadi, wet dream without wetness, birth without blood, penetration with a barrier, insertion of finger, bestiality, intercourse with a dead body without emission, intercourse with a virgin without breaking hymen.
The list is incomplete in the source; we rely on reliable copies.
4
Note the reason for each
Each case lacks certainty of emission or involves a barrier preventing direct contact or sensation.
5
Apply to a scenario
For example, a person who has a wet dream but finds no wetness does not need ghusl.

Chapter on what necessitates ghusl: (157) [Fluid] emitted before sleep? and (158) finding wetness thought to be mani after recovering from intoxication or unconsciousness. And due to menstruation and lochia, ghusl will not be obligatory, but if before sleep, despite emission of fluid, it becomes certain that it is mani water, then ghusl will be obligatory because it is known with certainty that emission occurred. Proof: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about a man who finds wetness but does not remember a wet dream? He said: He should perform ghusl. And about a man who sees that he had a wet dream but does not find wetness? He said: No ghusl upon him. (Tirmidhi, chapter on one who wakes up and finds wetness but does not remember a wet dream, p.30 no.113; Abu Dawud, chapter on a man who finds wetness in his sleep, p.44 no.236). This hadith indicates that if there is certainty of mani emission, ghusl is obligatory; if there is doubt, ghusl is not obligatory. Translation (157): [5] The presence of wetness after regaining consciousness from intoxication or unconsciousness, when it is the dominant presumption that it is mani. Explanation: Intoxication and unconsciousness are like sleep because in them the intellect is impaired. Therefore, after regaining consciousness from intoxication or unconsciousness, if one sees wetness on the body or clothes and the dominant presumption is that mani came out, then ghusl becomes obligatory because the person has become junub. Translation (158): [1] After menstruation and lochia, and the correct narration is that if these things occurred before embracing Islam, [even then ghusl is necessary]. Explanation: After menstruation and lochia end, ghusl becomes obligatory. If menstruation and lochia occurred before embracing Islam and one had not performed ghusl and then became Muslim, even then ghusl is obligatory because the cause of ghusl existed. Proof: (1) They ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they purify themselves. And when they have purified themselves, then come to them from where Allah has commanded you. (Quran 2:222) The verse indicates that a menstruating woman should perform ghusl before intercourse. (2) Hadith: From Aisha that a woman asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about her ghusl from menstruation? He ordered her how to perform ghusl. He said: Take a piece of musk and purify yourself with it, etc. (Bukhari, chapter on a woman rubbing herself when purifying from menstruation, p.25 no.1314; Muslim, chapter on the desirability of a woman bathing from menstruation using a piece of musk, p.147 no.3232/738). This hadith shows that ghusl is obligatory upon a menstruating woman. (3) From Mu'adh from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: When seven days have passed for the woman in lochia, then if she sees purity, let her perform ghusl and pray. (Mustadrak al-Hakim, book of purification, vol.1 p.284 no.626; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on lochia, p.505 no.1617). This hadith shows that a woman in lochia should also perform ghusl after the blood ends. Translation (159): And washing the deceased is a communal obligation. Chapter on things from which ghusl is not performed. And if the mentioned things occurred before Islam, according to the correct view (159), and it is obligatory to wash the deceased as a communal obligation. Chapter: Ten things from which ghusl is not performed. Explanation: This ghusl is a communal obligation, meaning if some people perform the ghusl, it suffices on behalf of all. And since it is not an individual obligation, the author did not count it. Proof: (1) In this hadith: From Umm Atiyya al-Ansariyya said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) entered upon us when his daughter died and said: Wash her three times, or five times, or more than that if you see fit, with water and sidr, and put camphor in the last. (Bukhari, chapter on washing the deceased and their ablution with water and sidr, p.201 no.1253; Muslim, chapter on washing the deceased, p.1377 no.2168/939). This hadith indicates that the deceased should be washed, and another woman washed her, and it sufficed on behalf of the Prophet; this is evidence that it is a communal obligation. Chapter: Ten things from which ghusl is not performed. Ten things from which ghusl is not obligatory, at a glance: Madhy, Wadi, wet dream without wetness, and according to the correct madhhab, birth of a child without seeing blood, and penetration with a cloth that prevents the sensation of pleasure, and insertion of a finger etc. into one of the two passages, an animal, or intercourse with a deceased without emission, ... intercourse with a virgin without emission such that her hymen is not removed. ☆☆☆
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section from the chapter on ghusl in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by stating the causes that necessitate ghusl: emission of mani (with certainty), finding wetness after unconsciousness/intoxication with dominant presumption, and after menstruation/lochia. He then provides a hadith from Aisha (RA) establishing that certainty of mani necessitates ghusl, while doubt does not. The commentary clarifies that the ruling applies whether the person was asleep, intoxicated, or unconscious, as the intellect is impaired in all these states. The Quranic verse (2:222) and additional hadith are cited to prove that ghusl is obligatory after menstruation and lochia. The passage then transitions to the ruling that washing the deceased is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), supported by the hadith of Umm Atiyya. Finally, the chapter lists ten things that do not necessitate ghusl, though the list is incomplete in the text. The author explains that since ghusl for the deceased is not an individual obligation, it was not counted among the obligatory ghusls earlier. The list includes madhy, wadi, wet dream without wetness, birth without blood, penetration with a barrier, insertion of finger, bestiality, intercourse with a dead body without emission, and intercourse with a virgin without breaking the hymen. These are all cases where ghusl is not wajib because there is no certainty or emission of mani.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the entire body.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): Communal obligation.
مذي (madhy): Prostatic fluid that does not necessitate ghusl.
ودي (wadi): Thick urine discharge that does not necessitate ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, washing a deceased Muslim is:
A) Fard ayn (individual obligation)
B) Fard kifayah (communal obligation)
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Washing the deceased is a communal obligation; many acts, like madhy or wet dream without wetness, do not require ghusl.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Ten Things That Do Not Require Ghusl: Rulings and Proofs
Listing acts and discharges that do not obligate ritual bath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which discharges require only wudu (madhi, wadi) and which require ghusl, and explain the Hanafi proofs for these rulings.

Core Idea
Ghusl is only for semen or intercourse; madhi and wadi require only wudu.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text lists ten things that do not require ghusl (full ablution). The author emphasizes that ghusl is only obligatory for two causes: emission of semen or direct sexual intercourse. For other discharges and acts, only wudu suffices or nothing at all. The text provides clear hadith evidence for the first three items: madhi (pre-ejaculate), wadi (post-urine fluid), and a wet dream without moisture. Understanding these distinctions is essential for everyday ritual purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the list of ten things. For each, determine whether the passage says ghusl is not required. Note that the first three items (madhi, wadi, ihtilam without moisture) are explained with proofs.
The passage also includes a general principle: ghusl is only due to semen emission or complete intercourse.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the three proofs cited: hadith of Ali on madhi, statement of Aisha on wadi, and hadith of Umm Sulaym on wet dream. Identify their sources (Bukhari, Abu Dawud, Muslim, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah).
These are ahad hadiths but accepted as evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative 'توضأ' (perform wudu) in the madhi hadith indicates that only wudu is required, not ghusl. For wet dream, the phrase 'اذا رأت الماء' (if she sees water) shows that ghusl depends on actual emission.
The statement of Aisha directly says 'from madhi and wadi, one performs wudu'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage says 'في الصحيح' (in the correct view) for childbirth without blood, implying a disagreement within the school. The other items are largely agreed upon in the Hanafi school.
Some earlier Hanafis may have differed on childbirth.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that all ten items do not require ghusl. For childbirth without bleeding, the correct view is that ghusl is not required because no nifas blood emerged.
This tarjih is consistent with the general principles.

Chapter: Ten things from which ghusl is not performed
Section: Ten things from which ghusl is not performed
10 things from which ghusl is not obligatory, in one view:
1. Madhi.
2. Wadi.
3. Wet dream without moisture.
4. And in the correct madhhab: childbirth after it without seeing blood.
5. And entering with a cloth that prevents sensation.
6. And inserting a finger or something into one of the two passages.
7. A quadruped.
8. Or having intercourse with a corpse without emission.
9. ... with a virgin in such a way without emission that her hymen is not removed.
☆☆☆
(160). Madhi, wadi, and wet dream without moisture (161) and childbirth without seeing blood after it, in the correct view (162) Principle: If complete intercourse occurs, ghusl becomes obligatory. Principle: If semen comes out, ghusl becomes obligatory. In the following ten situations, these two conditions are not present, so ghusl is not obligatory. Translation: (120) [1] Madhi [2] Wadi [3] Wet dream without moisture. Explanation: Madhi and wadi do not require ghusl, rather only wudu is required. He should wash the madhi and wadi and perform wudu. Similarly, if in sleep he imagined that he had a wet dream but there is no moisture on the clothes or body, that means semen did not come out, so ghusl is not obligatory.
Allah (swt)
Proof: (1) From Ali (ra) who said: I was a man who emitted much madhi, so I asked a man to ask the Prophet (saw)... He asked and he (the Prophet) said: Perform wudu and wash your penis. (Bukhari, Book of Ghusl of Madhi and Wudu from it, p.48, no.269; Abu Dawood, Book on Madhi, p.131, no.206) In this hadith, there is wudu for madhi, not ghusl. (2) Ghusl is not obligatory for wadi, only wudu is obligatory. For this, there is the statement of a companion: From Aisha (ra) who said: For semen, there is ghusl; for madhi and wadi, one performs wudu from both. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Book on Semen, Madhi, and Wadi, vol.1, p.88, no.977) In this statement of a companion, there is wudu for wadi and madhi. (3) As for wet dream, if semen comes out, then ghusl is obligatory; otherwise not. For this, there is this hadith: Umm Sulaym, the wife of Abu Talha, came to the Messenger of Allah (saw) and said: O Messenger of Allah, indeed Allah is not shy of the truth. Does a woman have to perform ghusl if she has a wet dream? The Messenger of Allah (saw) said: Yes, if she sees water. (Bukhari, Book When a Woman has a Wet Dream, p.50, no.282; Muslim, Book on Obligation of Ghusl for Woman due to Emission of Semen, p.145, no.712/313) Lexicon: Madhi is water that comes out from the penis during foreplay with a woman. And wadi is a thin water that comes out after urination. For both, wudu is required. Ihtilam is derived from 'jilm' (semen), meaning a dream, during sleep semen comes out, that is ihtilam.
Allah (swt)
Translation: (161) (2) Childbirth without seeing blood, ghusl is not obligatory. In the correct madhhab. Explanation: A child was born but after it absolutely no blood came out, so ghusl is not obligatory for this woman. The correct madhhab is this. Reason: The reason is that ghusl becomes obligatory due to the blood of nifas coming out, and here blood did not come out at all, so ghusl will not be obligatory. Translation: (162) [5] And entering with a cloth that prevents sensation.
Explanation: That thick cloth such that the heat of the private part and sensation cannot be obtained, wrapping the penis in such cloth and (entering) into the vagina...
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section listing ten things that do not obligate ghusl in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that there are ten things from which ghusl is not performed, and then enumerates them. The first three are madhi, wadi, and a wet dream without any moisture. For these, the author provides clear proofs: a hadith from Ali (ra) regarding madhi, a statement of Aisha (ra) for wadi, and a hadith from Umm Sulaym for wet dream. The key principle is that ghusl is only obligatory for the release of semen (maniy) or for direct sexual intercourse with penetration. The remaining items in the list are variations that lack either complete intercourse or seminal emission: childbirth without post-natal bleeding (since nifas blood did not flow), intercourse with a barrier (thick cloth that prevents sensation), insertion of a finger, intercourse with an animal, with a corpse without emission, and with a virgin without penetration of the hymen. The author notes that the ruling on childbirth is 'the correct view' (al-sahih), implying some disagreement within the school. The overall message is that Hanafi fiqh is precise in distinguishing between fluids and acts that necessitate a full bath versus those that require only wudu.

Key Terms
مذي (madhi): Water that comes out from the penis during foreplay with a woman; it requires wudu but not ghusl.
ودي (wadi): Thin water that comes out after urination; it requires wudu but not ghusl.
احتلام (ihtilam): A dream during sleep in which semen is emitted; ghusl is required only if moisture (semen) is seen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following requires ghusl?
A) Emission of madhi during foreplay
B) Wet dream without seeing any moisture on clothes
C) Childbirth without any post-natal bleeding
D) Ejaculation of semen during sleep while seeing moisture

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ghusl is limited to semen emission and sexual intercourse; madhi, wadi, and childbirth without blood do not require it.

The Ruling on Madhiy, Wadiy, and Ihtilam without Wetness
States three cases that do not require ghusl with proofs and linguistic definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for madhiy, wadiy, and ihtilam without wetness, and cite the primary evidence for each.

Core Idea
Madhiy and wadiy only require wudu, not ghusl; ihtilam without wetness requires nothing.

This passage addresses a common point of confusion: when does a discharge or nocturnal emission obligate ghusl? The author establishes two general principles—ghusl is required for full intercourse or emission of mani—then lists three specific cases where neither occurs, ruling that ghusl is not required. By understanding these distinctions, you will be able to correctly determine when ghusl is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two general causes of ghusl
The passage begins with two principles: complete intercourse and emission of mani. These are the bases for ghusl obligation.
These are the only two triggers for ghusl.
2
List the three exceptions
Madhiy, wadiy, and ihtilam without wetness. The passage states that in these cases, neither intercourse nor mani emission occurs, so ghusl is not required.
The rule of exceptions confirms the general principles.
3
Examine the evidence for madhiy
The hadith from Ali (ra) where the Prophet commanded wudu and washing the organ, not ghusl.
The imperative 'توضأ' (perform wudu) indicates obligation of wudu, and absence of ghusl command indicates it is not required.
4
Examine the evidence for wadiy
The statement of Aisha (ra) that from mani is ghusl, and from madhiy and wadiy one performs wudu.
This is a qawl sahabi, considered a source of evidence in Hanafi school.
5
Examine the evidence for ihtilam without wetness
The hadith of Umm Sulaym where the Prophet said 'if she sees water', conditioning ghusl on seeing water (mani).
If no wetness, no mani, so no ghusl.

Chapter: What does not require ghusl. (160) Madhiy, wadiy, and ihtilam without wetness. (161) Childbirth without seeing blood after it, according to the correct view. (162) Principle: If complete intercourse takes place, ghusl is required. Principle: If mani is emitted, ghusl is obligatory. In the following ten cases, neither of these two situations exists, so ghusl is not fard. Translation: (120) [1] Madhiy [2] Wadiy [3] Ihtilam without wetness. Explanation: Ghusl is not required for the emission of madhiy and wadiy; only wudu is required. Wash the madhiy and wadiy and perform wudu. Similarly, if during sleep one thinks he had a wet dream but finds no wetness on clothes or body, it means mani was not emitted, so ghusl is not required. Proof: (1) Narrated by Ali: 'I was a man who emitted madhiy frequently, so I asked a man to ask the Prophet (peace be upon him) ... He said: Perform wudu and wash your penis.' (Bukhari, Abwab Ghusl al-Madhiy, and Abu Dawood). This hadith indicates that for madhiy there is wudu, not ghusl. (2) Wadiy does not require ghusl, only wudu. For this, the statement of Aisha: 'From mani is ghusl, and from madhiy and wadiy one performs wudu.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). (3) For ihtilam, if mani is emitted, then ghusl is obligatory; otherwise not. For this, the hadith: Umm Sulaym came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, does a woman have to perform ghusl if she has a wet dream? He said: Yes, if she sees water. (Bukhari and Muslim). Linguistic notes: Madhiy is the fluid that comes out during foreplay; wadiy is the thin fluid that comes after urine; for both, wudu is required. Ihtilam is derived from 'hilm' (dream), meaning emission of mani during sleep.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof passage. The author first states the general principle that ghusl is required for full intercourse (complete insertion) or emission of mani. Then he lists three specific cases where neither condition is present: madhiy (prostatic fluid), wadiy (thin discharge after urine), and nocturnal emission without any wetness. For each, he provides evidence: for madhiy, a hadith from Ali instructing wudu and washing the organ, not ghusl; for wadiy, the statement of Aisha that madhiy and wadiy require only wudu; for ihtilam without wetness, the hadith of Umm Sulaym where the Prophet conditioned ghusl on seeing water (i.e., emission of mani). The commentary then gives linguistic definitions, explaining that madhiy comes during foreplay, wadiy after urine, and ihtilam is emission of mani in sleep. The overall ruling is that these do not obligate ghusl, only wudu for madhiy and wadiy and nothing for ihtilam without wetness.

Key Terms
مذی (madhiy): Thin, white fluid emitted during foreplay; not requiring ghusl but requiring wudu.
ودی (wadiy): Thin fluid emitted after urination; not requiring ghusl but requiring wudu.
احتلام (ihtilam): Nocturnal emission; requires ghusl only if mani is seen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Statement of Aisha (ra)

Key Takeaway
Madhiy and wadiy require wudu but not ghusl; ihtilam without wetness requires neither, as ghusl is only for mani or full intercourse.

Ghusl After Childbirth Without Postpartum Blood
States that ghusl is not required for childbirth if no blood is seen postpartum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl after childbirth when no postpartum blood appears and explain the legal reason (talil) that ties ghusl obligation to the presence of nifas blood.

Core Idea
Ghusl after childbirth is obligatory only if nifas blood flows; no blood means no obligation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on ghusl after childbirth when no postpartum blood appears. The ruling is straightforward: ghusl is not required because its cause (sabab) is the flow of nifas blood. The passage provides a clear talil (reason) that the obligation is tied to the existence of blood. Understanding this principle prevents unnecessary ritual burdens and clarifies the legal link between cause and ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is childbirth (nifas). The ruling explicitly states that ghusl is not wajib when no blood is seen. Note that the ruling is conditional on the absence of blood.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides a talil: ghusl becomes wajib due to nifas blood. This is the legal cause (sabab) for the obligation. In this case, since no blood came out, the cause is absent.
The dalil is a rational inference from the general rule that ghusl for nifas is triggered by blood.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning is direct: the ruling (wujub ghusl) follows the presence of its cause (nifas blood). This is an application of the Hanafi principle that obligations are contingent upon their causes. The absence of blood necessarily means no obligation.
This is a clear case of talil: a cause-effect relationship, not an analogy.
4
Note the madhhab confirmation
The text states this is 'the correct madhhab' (sahih mazhab). This indicates that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that no ghusl is required. Some historical differences may have existed, but the mufta bihi is settled.
The phrase 'پیچ مذہب یہی ہے' is a variant spelling of 'صحیح مذہب یہی ہے' (this is the correct madhhab).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that ghusl is not obligatory when no nifas blood appears. This is consistent across the Zahir al-Riwayah and is followed by later Hanafi scholars. The ruling is based on a clear cause-and-effect link.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded for this specific point; all three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۶۱) (۲) بچہ پیدا ہونے کے بعد بغیر خون دیکھے ہوئے غسل واجب نہیں ہے۔ صحیح مذہب میں۔ تشریح : بچہ پیدا ہوا لیکن اس کے بعد قطعا کوئی خون نہیں نکلا تو اس عورت پر غسل واجب نہیں ہے، پیچ مذہب یہی ہے ۔ وجہ : اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ غسل واجب ہوتا ہے نفاس کے خون نکلنے سے اور یہاں خون نکلا ہی نہیں اس لئے غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا
Translation: (161) (2) After childbirth without seeing blood, ghusl is not obligatory, according to the correct madhhab. Explanation: A woman gave birth but no blood came out at all afterwards; then ghusl is not obligatory for her. This is the correct madhhab. Reason: The reason is that ghusl becomes obligatory due to nifas blood, and here no blood came out, so ghusl is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a ruling with reason (talil) passage. The author clarifies that after childbirth, if no blood (nifas) is seen, ghusl is not required. The reason is that the obligation of ghusl for postpartum women is tied to the flow of nifas blood; if there is no blood, the cause for ghusl is absent. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school (al-sahih).

Key Terms
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding; the blood that causes obligation of ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ghusl After Intercourse Through a Pleasure-Preventing Barrier
Ruling on ghusl after intercourse with a thick barrier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl when intercourse occurs through a pleasure-preventing barrier and identify the condition that makes ghusl wajib.

Core Idea
Ghusl is not obligatory when a barrier prevents genital pleasure unless ejaculation occurs.

In this passage, the author addresses a common scenario: what if intercourse is performed with a thick cloth that blocks all sensation? The Hanafi school distinguishes between full genital contact with pleasure and mere mechanical insertion. The ruling emphasizes that the obligation of ghusl is tied to either direct genital pleasure or emission of mani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize the scenario: intercourse with a thick barrier that prevents pleasure. The ruling is that ghusl is not wajib.
2
Locate the condition for obligation
Determine what would make ghusl wajib here: emission of mani (ejaculation).
3
Understand the reasoning
The author compares this to intercourse outside the vagina because the pleasure of the private part is not obtained. Hence, only mani triggers ghusl.
4
Apply the same to modern materials
The rule applies equally to thick rubber (e.g., thick condoms that prevent all sensation).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that mere insertion of the glans (hashafah) into the vagina requires ghusl, even without pleasure or ejaculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۶۲) [۵] اور ایسے کپڑے سے دخول کرنا جو وجود لذت سے مانع ہو۔ تشریح : اتنا موٹا کپڑا ہے کہ شرمگاہ کی حرارت اور لذت حاصل نہیں ہوسکتی، عضوتناسل کو ایسے کپڑے میں لپیٹ کر شرمگاہ میں داخل کیا تو صرف حشفہ چھپنے سے غسل واجب نہیں ہو گا جب تک کہ منی نہ نکل جائے، کیونکہ جب شرمگاہ کی لذت حاصل نہیں ہوئی تو گویا کہ شرمگاہ کے علاوہ میں وطی کی ، اس لئے منی نہ نکلنے سے غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ یہی حال موٹے ربر کا ہے۔
Translation: (162) [5] And insertion with a cloth that prevents the existence of pleasure. Explanation: It is such a thick cloth that the heat and pleasure of the private part cannot be obtained. If the male organ is wrapped in such a cloth and inserted into the vagina, then merely concealing the glans does not make ghusl obligatory as long as mani does not come out, because when the pleasure of the private part is not obtained, it is as if intercourse took place outside the vagina. Therefore, if mani is not emitted, ghusl is not obligatory. The same applies to a thick rubber.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a ruling statement passage. The author explains that if intercourse is performed with a very thick cloth or rubber that prevents the sensation of pleasure, then ghusl becomes obligatory only if mani is emitted. If no ejaculation occurs, ghusl is not required, even if the glans is concealed. The reason is that the pleasure and heat of the genitals are not exchanged, so it is akin to intercourse outside the vagina. This is based on the principle that ghusl is required either for full intercourse with pleasure or emission of mani; here neither exists.

Key Terms
حشفہ (hashafah): The glans of the penis; its concealment is considered the start of intercourse but ghusl is not required if pleasure is blocked.
منی (mani): Semen; its emission is one of the major impurities requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Wajib
B) Not wajib
C) Makruh
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Ghusl after intercourse is not obligatory when a thick barrier prevents pleasure and no ejaculation occurs.

Ruling on Enema and Ghusl
Ruling statement with brief reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl after an enema and explain the legal reasoning (illah) for the absence of obligation.

Core Idea
An enema does not require ghusl because the causes of janabah (intercourse or mani) are absent.

Medical procedures sometimes raise questions about ritual purity. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on enema: it is a cleansing of the intestines, not an act that triggers major impurity. Understanding the underlying causes (asbab) of ghusl helps distinguish between what obligates ghusl and what does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'rightah lagana' (administering an enema). The ruling is that ghusl is not wajib (obligatory).
The Arabic text uses 'غل' for enema.
2
Locate the legal cause (illah)
The author states that the reason is that there is no intercourse or emission of mani (semen). These are the two classical causes of janabah in the Hanafi school.
Intercourse (jima') and ejaculation (inzal) are the only triggers for ghusl.
3
Apply the rule of absence of cause
Since the illah is missing, the ruling of ghusl being wajib does not apply. This is a straightforward application of the principle that the ruling follows its cause.
4
Contrast with acts that do require ghusl
For comparison, ghusl is wajib after sexual intercourse (even without ejaculation in the Hanafi school) and after ejaculation (whether from intercourse or otherwise).
This confirms that the absence of both triggers is decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۶۳) [۲] حقہ لگانے سے غسل واجب نہیں ہو گا ۔ وجه : آنت کی صفائی کے لئے پانی اور دوائی ڈال کر پیخانہ کے راستے سے حقہ لگاتے ہیں، چونکہ اس میں جماع یا منی کا نکلنا نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے اس سے غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔
Translation: (163) [2] Administering an enema does not make ghusl obligatory. Reason: Water and medicine are inserted into the rectum to clean the intestines. Since there is no intercourse or emission of mani, ghusl is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a ruling statement passage. The author clarifies that using an enema (injection of fluid into the rectum) does not require ghusl because it is a medical procedure, not an act of intercourse or a means of ejaculation. The cause for ghusl is absent.

Key Terms
حقہ (huqnah): An enema; injection of liquid into the rectum for medical purposes.
غسل (ghusl): Full-body ritual washing to remove major impurity (janabah).
جماع (jimā'): Sexual intercourse (penetration).
منی (manī): Semen, emitted during ejaculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is only obligatory when the specific causes (intercourse or ejaculation) are present; a medical enema does not trigger it.

Inserting Finger into Rectum or Vagina: No Ghusl Required
Ruling on inserting finger into one of the two passages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inserting a finger into the anus or vagina and explain why ghusl is not obligatory.

Core Idea
Ghusl is not obligatory for finger insertion as it is neither intercourse nor emission of mani.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the Hanafi school regarding what necessitates ghusl. The passage clarifies that inserting a finger or similar object into the private parts does not trigger the obligation of ghusl. Understanding this helps distinguish between different causes of major ritual impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is inserting a finger or similar into the anus or vagina. The ruling is that ghusl is not obligatory.
The ruling is explicit: no ghusl required.
2
Recall the causes of ghusl
In Hanafi fiqh, ghusl becomes wajib due to two causes: sexual intercourse (with insertion of the male organ) and emission of mani (with sexual desire).
These causes are derived from the Quran and Sunnah.
3
Apply the causes to the act
Inserting a finger does not constitute intercourse (no male organ involved) and typically does not lead to emission of mani. Thus, neither cause is present, so ghusl is not required.
If mani were emitted during insertion, then ghusl would be required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۶۴) (۷) اور انگلی و غیرہ کا احد السبیلین میں داخل کرنا۔ تشریح : پیخانہ کے راستے میں یا عورت کی شرمگاہ میں انگلی داخل کی تو اس سے نہ جماع پایا گیا اور نہ نی نکلی اس لئے اس سے بھی غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا۔
Translation: (164) (7) And inserting a finger or similar into one of the two passages. Explanation: If a finger is inserted into the rectum or into a woman's vagina, neither intercourse nor emission of mani occurred, so ghusl is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a ruling statement passage. The author rules that inserting a finger or similar object into the anus or vagina does not require ghusl, as it is not intercourse (which involves the male sexual organ) and does not typically cause ejaculation. The absence of both causes for ghusl leaves it non-obligatory.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath to remove major impurity (janabah).
منی (mani): Semen emitted with sexual desire, one of the causes for ghusl.
احد السبیلین (ahad al-sabilayn): One of the two passages: the anus and the vagina (front and back passages).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person inserts a finger into the rectum, is ghusl required?
A) Yes
B) No
C) Only if mani is emitted
D) Wudu is required

Key Takeaway
Inserting a finger into the anus or vagina does not obligate ghusl because it is neither intercourse nor emission of mani.

Ghusl Not Required for Intercourse with Animal or Corpse Without Ejaculation
Ruling on ghusl for bestiality/necrophilia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for bestiality/necrophilia without ejaculation and identify the conditions that trigger the obligation of ghusl.

Core Idea
Ghusl is only wajib from ejaculation or insertion into a living human.

This lesson clarifies a specific case: when a person engages in intercourse with an animal or a corpse but does not ejaculate. The Hanafi ruling is clear: ghusl is not required. Understanding this requires knowing the conditions that make ghusl obligatory — specifically, that the partner must be a living human for the insertion to trigger the obligation without ejaculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is intercourse (wati) with an animal or corpse without ejaculation. The ruling: ghusl is not wajib.
2
Understand the Rationale
The author gives the reason: the act does not involve insertion into the vagina or anus of a living human being. Therefore, the condition for ghusl (mutual pleasure or direct contact with a living human's private parts) is not met.
3
Recall the General Principle
In Hanafi fiqh, ghusl becomes wajib either by emission of mani (with or without insertion) or by insertion of the glans (hashingfa) into the vagina/anus of a living human. Here, neither condition is satisfied: no emission and the partner is not a living human.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some other schools may argue that bestiality is a form of zina and thus requires ghusl regardless. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the textual proofs that limit the obligation to living human partners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۶۵)[۸] چوپایہ [9] یا میت سے بغیر انزال کے وطی کرنے [ سے غسل واجب نہیں ہو گا ] وجه : چوپایہ سے دلی کرنے سے، یا میت سے ولی کرنے سے زندہ آدمی کی دبر یا قبل میں ولی کرنا نہیں پائی گئی اس لئے دونوں طرف سے لذت کا ملہ نہیں پائی گئی ، اس لئے صرف حشفہ کے چھپ جانے سے غسل واجب نہیں ہوگا جب تک کہ انزال نہ ہو جائے ۔ دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
Translation: (165) [8] Intercourse with an animal or a corpse without ejaculation [does not obligate ghusl]. Reason: When one commits bestiality or necrophilia, intercourse with the vagina or anus of a living person does not occur, so mutual pleasure is not attained. Therefore, merely concealing the glans does not necessitate ghusl until ejaculation occurs. The proof has already passed.

Commentary
This is a ruling statement passage. The author addresses the case of intercourse with an animal or a corpse without ejaculation. Since this is not intercourse with a living human being, the conditions for ghusl (insertion into a living human's vagina/anus with pleasure) are not fully met. Therefore, ghusl is not required unless mani is emitted. The author refers to an earlier proof (likely the general principle).

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual purification of the entire body required after janaba (major impurity).
جنابت (janaba): State of major ritual impurity caused by ejaculation or intercourse.
حشفہ (hashingfa): Glans of the penis; concealment of it in a living human's private part triggers ghusl.
انزال (inzal): Ejaculation of semen; one of the two causes of ghusl.

When Ghusl Is Not Required: Incomplete Penetration
Ruling and explanation of ghusl requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl after intercourse without full penetration and without ejaculation, and identify the condition of ghaybat al-hashafah (concealment of glans) as the threshold for ghusl obligation.

Core Idea
No ghusl without full penetration or ejaculation — the intact hymen signals incomplete entry.

Marital intimacy often begins gradually. A common question is whether ghusl becomes obligatory when there is contact but not full penetration. This passage from a Hanafi primer provides a clear ruling tied to two specific conditions. Understanding this helps avoid unnecessary ritual washing and clarifies the school's precise criteria.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intercourse with a virgin where the hymen remains intact and no ejaculation occurs. The ruling from the passage is that ghusl is not obligatory (wajib).
2
Understand the rationale
The hymen's intactness indicates that the male glans never became fully concealed inside the vagina (ghaybat al-hashafah). In Hanafi fiqh, this concealment is a necessary condition for ghusl when there is no ejaculation.
3
Apply the alternative condition
If either full penetration (glans concealed) OR ejaculation occurs, ghusl becomes wajib. This case lacks both conditions, so no ghusl is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۶۶)[۱۰] باکرہ سے اس طرح بلا انزال جماع کرے کہ اس کی بکارت زائل نہ ہو۔ تشریح : باکرہ عورت کی شرمگاہ میں ختنہ کے مقام پر پردہ بکارت ہوتی ہے، پس اگر اس طرح اس سے وطی کی کہ پردہ بکارت زائل نہیں ہوئی تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ مرد کا عضو تناسل عورت کے ختنے کے اندر داخل نہیں ہوا ، اور شرمگاہ میں حشفہ غائب نہیں ہوا۔ اس لئے جب تک کہ انزال نہ ہو غسل واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ لغت : ایلاج : ولج سے مشتق ہے۔ داخل کرنا۔ خرقہ : کپڑے کا ٹکڑا۔ حقنہ پیخانہ کے راستے میں ڈوائی ڈال کر صاف کرنا۔ اصابتہ : پہنچنا، یہاں مراد ہے، وطی کرنا۔ بکارۃ : پردہ بکارت ۔
Translation: (166) [10] Intercourse with a virgin without ejaculation in such a way that her hymen is not removed. Explanation: A virgin woman has a hymen at the spot of circumcision. So if one has intercourse with her in a way that the hymen is not removed, this means that the male organ did not enter inside the circumcision of the woman, and the glans was not concealed in the vagina. Therefore, as long as ejaculation does not occur, ghusl is not obligatory. Linguistic notes: Ilaaj: derived from walaja, meaning to enter. Khirqah: piece of cloth. Huqnah: cleaning the rectum with medicine. Isabah: to reach, here meaning intercourse. Bakaarah: hymen.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a ruling statement passage with linguistic notes. The author explains that if a man has intercourse with a virgin woman but does not break the hymen (i.e., the male organ does not fully penetrate into the vagina where the glans becomes concealed), and no ejaculation occurs, then ghusl is not required. This is because the condition of 'concealment of the glans in a living human's vagina' is not met. The linguistic notes define terms used in the section: Ilaaj (insertion), Khirqah (cloth), Huqnah (enema), Isabah (intercourse), and Bakaarah (hymen).

Key Terms
بکارۃ (bakaarah): The hymen, a membrane at the entrance of a virgin's vagina.
حشفہ (hashafah): The glans of the penis.
ایلاج (ilaaj): Insertion, entry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes
B) No
C) Only wudu is required
D) Ghusl is mustahabb

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of ghusl after intimacy is tied to either full concealment of the glans (ghaybat al-hashafah) or ejaculation; without both, ghusl is not required.

Cases Where Ghusl Is Not Wajib: Chapter on Exceptions
Listing five exceptions to ghusl obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five cases where ghusl is not obligatory according to the Hanafi school and explain the underlying principle (absence of direct genital pleasure or ejaculation).

Core Idea
Ghusl is not wajib if there is no direct genital pleasure and no ejaculation — mere insertion is insufficient.

In the previous lesson we learned the causes of ghusl: direct genital contact (iltiqā' al-khātanayn) and ejaculation (inzal). But what happens when there is insertion without these two factors? This lesson presents five specific scenarios from the Hanafi fiqh text where ghusl is not required. The common thread is that neither direct pleasure nor semen emission is present. Understanding these exceptions is crucial to avoid unnecessary ritual baths and to correctly apply the school's rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five exceptions
Read through the passage and list the five cases where ghusl is not obligatory: (1) insertion with a cloth preventing pleasure, (2) enema, (3) inserting a finger into either passage, (4) intercourse with an animal or corpse without ejaculation, (5) intercourse with a virgin without breaking the hymen.
Each case is numbered in the translation (163-166).
2
Extract the common legal principle
Notice that in all cases, there is either no direct genital contact (e.g., finger, enema, cloth barrier) or no living human partner (animal/corpse, hymen intact). The key is that the glans (hashafah) does not enter a living human vagina or anus without a barrier.
The Hanafi rule: ghusl becomes wajib either by direct contact (glans to living human private part without barrier) or by ejaculation. If both are absent, ghusl is not wajib.
3
Analyze the reasoning for each case
For each case, state the specific reason given in the text. Example: Enema – no intercourse or ejaculation; finger – no intercourse or ejaculation; animal/corpse – no mutual pleasure; virgin with intact hymen – glans did not enter the vagina.
The text repeatedly emphasizes the absence of pleasure (ladhdha) and ejaculation.
4
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Consider a modern scenario: a person uses a condom and does not ejaculate. Does ghusl become wajib? According to the principle, the condom acts like the cloth barrier, preventing direct sensation, and without ejaculation, ghusl is not wajib.
This is a direct application of the first exception (إيلاج بخِرقة).
5
Memorize the list for exam recall
Commit the five cases to memory. Use the mnemonic: 'Cloth, enema, finger, animal/corpse, virgin intact'.
These are standard examples in Hanafi fiqh for when ghusl is not required.

Chapter: What does not require ghusl. Thamaratun Najah volume 1: Insertion with a cloth preventing the existence of pleasure (163), an enema (164), insertion of a finger or similar into one of the two passages (165), intercourse with an animal or a corpse without ejaculation (166), and having intercourse with a virgin whose virginity has not been removed without ejaculation. If he inserts, then merely covering the glans does not make ghusl obligatory until semen comes out, because when pleasure of the private part is not obtained, it is as if intercourse was done elsewhere; therefore, without semen emission, ghusl is not obligatory. The same applies to a thick rubber. Translation: (163) [2] Ghusl is not obligatory by applying an enema. Reason: Enema is given through the anal passage to clean the intestines with water and medicine; since neither intercourse nor ejaculation occurred, ghusl is not obligatory. Translation: (164) (7) And inserting a finger or similar into one of the two passages. Explanation: If he inserts a finger into the anal passage or the woman's private part, then neither intercourse occurred nor did semen come out, so also from this ghusl is not obligatory. Translation: (165)[8] Intercourse with an animal or a corpse without ejaculation [does not necessitate ghusl]. Reason: Because from intercourse with an animal or a corpse, the intercourse with the anus or vagina of a living person is not found; therefore, mutual pleasure is not obtained. Hence, merely covering the glans does not make ghusl obligatory unless ejaculation occurs. The proof has passed earlier. Translation: (166)[10] He has intercourse with a virgin without ejaculation in such a way that her hymen is not removed. Explanation: A virgin woman has a hymen at the site of circumcision in her private part. Thus, if he has intercourse with her in a way that the hymen is not removed, this means that the male organ did not enter inside the circumcision area of the woman, and the glans did not disappear in the private part. Therefore, ghusl is not obligatory until ejaculation occurs. Vocabulary: Ilaj: derived from walaja, meaning to insert. Khirqah: a piece of cloth. Huqnah: cleaning by inserting medicine into the anal passage. Isabah: reaching, here meaning intercourse. Bakarah: hymen.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi fiqh text listing cases where ghusl (ritual bath) is not wajib. The chapter 'ما لا يغتسل منه' covers five specific scenarios: (1) inserting the private part covered by a thick cloth that prevents pleasure, (2) administering an enema, (3) inserting a finger into the anus or vagina, (4) intercourse with an animal or a dead body, and (5) intercourse with a virgin without breaking the hymen. In all these cases, ghusl is not wajib unless ejaculation occurs. The reasoning is that mere insertion of the glans (hashafah) does not necessitate ghusl unless there is actual pleasure of the private parts or semen emission. The author draws a parallel to intercourse with a living human — if the glans is covered and no pleasure is felt, it is similar to having intercourse with something other than the private part. The enema and finger insertion do not involve intercourse, so ghusl is not required. For animals and corpses, there is no mutual pleasure, so the same ruling applies. For a virgin, if the hymen remains intact, it means the glans did not enter the vagina, so ghusl is not wajib without ejaculation. The proof for these rulings is referenced as having passed earlier in the text.

Key Terms
ایلاج (īlāj): Insertion, especially of the male organ into a passage.
حقنة (huqnah): An enema, the injection of liquid into the rectum for purgation.
اصابة (iṣābah): Reaching, used here to mean intercourse or contact.
بكارۃ (bakārah): The hymen, the membrane partially covering the vaginal opening in a virgin.
خرقة (khirqah): A piece of cloth, used here as a barrier.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ghusl is not wajib when both direct genital contact (without barrier) and ejaculation are absent; mere insertion or non-genital acts do not necessitate the ritual bath.

The Eleven Obligatory Acts of Ghusl: A Hanafi Ruling
Listing the eleven obligatory acts in the ritual bath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list all eleven fard acts of ghusl according to the Hanafi school and explain the Quranic basis for their obligation.

Core Idea
In ghusl, eleven acts are fard; every spot from head to toe must be washed, including hidden areas like the navel and prepuce.

This passage from a classical Hanafi text enumerates the obligatory acts of the ritual bath (ghusl). While the Quran commands a general purification, the Hanafi school details eleven specific requirements to ensure complete coverage. Understanding these fard acts is essential for valid worship, as omitting any one invalidates the ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eleven fard acts
List each obligatory act mentioned in the passage: rinsing mouth, snuffing nose, washing entire body once, washing inside prepuce (if easily uncovered), washing navel, washing any open perforation, washing roots of man's matted hair, washing skin under beard, mustache, eyebrows, and washing external private parts.
The passage also mentions exceptions for women's braids.
2
Categorize the acts
Group them into body parts: head and face (mouth, nose, skin under facial hair), internal hidden areas (navel, prepuce, perforations), and general body surface.
The aim is to ensure no spot remains dry.
3
Locate the scriptural basis
Note the Quranic verse cited: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' (5:6). The Hanafi school considers this imperative to demand thorough washing, thus making each listed act fard.
The imperative 'fathharu' implies obligation according to Hanafi usul.
4
Note the special exceptions
The text states that a woman's braided hair does not need to be undone if water reaches the roots. This is based on a hadith. Also, washing inside the prepuce is only required if it can be opened without difficulty.
These exceptions prevent undue hardship.

...... اور فرج خارج کا دھونا۔
ترجمه : (۱۲۷) غسل میں گیارہ چیزیں فرض ہیں۔ [1] کلی کرنا، (۲) ناک میں پانی ڈالنا۔ [۳] ایک مرتبہ پورے بدن کا دھونا ۔
تشریح : غسل میں گیارہ چیزیں فرض ہیں انکی اصل بنیاد یہ ہے کہ آیت میں ہے کہ خوب خوب دھو وہ اس لئے بدن کے ہر ہر مقام پر پانی پہنچانا ضروری ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ منہ اور ناک کو نسل کے اندر جسم کے باہر کا حصہ قرار دیا، اور کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا فرض قرار دیا ۔ اسی طرح قلفہ، اور فرج خارج، اور بال کی جڑ ، ان تمام جگہوں پر پانی پہنچانا ضروری ہے ، حدیث کی بنا پر صرف عورت کے جوڑے میں پانی پہنچانا ضروری نہیں ہے ۔ تاکہ کہیں ایک بال کے برابر بھی خشک نہ رہ جائے۔ وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ وان كنتم جنبا فاطهروا ( آیت ۶ ، سورة المائدة (۵) آیت میں ہے کہ جنابت کی حالت میں
Chapter: Eleven things are obligatory in ghusl: (167) Washing the mouth, the nose, and the body once. The 11 obligatory acts of washing at a glance: Rinsing the mouth. Pouring water into the nose. ... Washing the entire body once. Chapter: In ghusl, eleven things are obligatory: And washing the inside of the prepuce which can be opened without difficulty. ... And washing the inside of the navel. And washing any perforation that is not closed. Chapter on the obligatory acts of ghusl: And absolutely washing the matted hair of a man, but not the matted hair of a woman when water reaches its root. ... And the skin of the beard. ... And the skin of the mustache. ... And the skin of the eyebrows. ... And washing the external private part. Translation: (127) Eleven things are obligatory in ghusl: [1] Rinsing the mouth, (2) Pouring water into the nose, [3] Washing the entire body once. Explanation: In ghusl, eleven things are obligatory; their basic principle is that the verse says 'wash thoroughly', therefore it is necessary to make water reach every place of the body. For this reason, the mouth and nose are considered as external parts of the body inside the lineage, and rinsing and snuffing are made obligatory. Similarly, the prepuce, the external private part, and the hair roots—making water reach all these places is necessary; based on hadith, it is not necessary to make water reach the braided hair of a woman. So that not even a hair's breadth remains dry. Reason: (1) The verse says: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' (Quran 5:6).
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi fiqh text explaining the obligatory (fard) acts of ghusl. It lists eleven obligatory elements: rinsing the mouth (madh-madah), snuffing water into the nose (istinshaq), washing the whole body once, washing the inside of the prepuce (qulfah) if easily uncovered, washing the navel cavity, washing any open wound or perforation, washing the roots of a man's matted hair (but not a woman's braids if water reaches the roots), washing the skin under the beard, mustache, and eyebrows, and washing the external private parts (farj kharij). The commentator explains that the Quranic command 'fathharu' (purify yourselves) from Surah al-Ma'idah implies washing every part thoroughly. The mouth and nose are considered external parts because they are openings of the body, so they must be washed. The exception for women's braids is based on a hadith that allows water to be poured over the head without untying the hair, provided water reaches the roots. The overall principle is that no spot, even the size of a hair, should remain dry. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قلفہ (qulfah): The prepuce or foreskin of the male; in ghusl, its interior must be washed if it can be easily retracted.
فرج خارج (farj khārij): The external part of the private parts (both male and female) that is visible; it must be washed in ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is rinsing the mouth (madmadah) considered obligatory in ghusl?
A) Because it is a sunnah of the Prophet (PBUH)
B) Because the mouth is considered an external part of the body
C) Because it removes bad breath
D) Because it is a requirement for validity of prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school makes eleven specific acts obligatory in ghusl, based on the Quranic command of thorough purification and the Sunnah, with the exception of a woman's braided hair if water reaches the roots.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
The Eleven Obligatory Acts of Ghusl
Enumeration of obligatory acts in ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eleven obligatory acts of ghusl according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for including the mouth and nose as fard.

Core Idea
Ghusl requires washing every external part, including mouth, nose, and hidden areas, or the purification is void.

The ritual bath (ghusl) is essential for purification from major ritual impurity. The Hanafi school specifies eleven obligatory acts that must be performed for the ghusl to be valid. This lesson presents that list and the evidence that supports it, highlighting the difference from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that ghusl has specific obligatory elements (fara'id). Each item listed is individually fard; omitting any invalidates the ghusl.
The text opens by stating there are eleven obligatory things.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the Quranic command in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6) 'And if you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves thoroughly.' Supplemental hadith emphasize washing every hair and spot.
The hadith 'Under every hair is janabah' is often cited.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fa-tahharu' indicates obligation. The inclusion of mouth and nose is based on their being external passages; hadith require water to reach roots of hair and skin.
Hanafis define external as what is visible or accessible without cutting.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools do not consider mouth and nose as fard, counting only intention, washing the entire body, and removing impurities.
The difference arises from how 'external' is defined.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Hanafis rely on a hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) rinsed his mouth and nose in ghusl, and the principle that any part that can be seen or accessed without hardship must be washed.
The mufta bihi position is the eleven listed items.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : ( يفترض في الاغتسال احد عشر شيئا . (١٦٧) غسل الفم والانف والبدن مرة . (١٦٨) وداخل قلفة لا عسر فى فسخها وسرة وثقب غير منضم . ومطلقا شعر الرجل المعقود إذا وصل الماء إلى أصوله وبشرى اللحية والشارب والحاجب وفرج خارج .
Section: Eleven things are obligatory in the ritual bath: (167) Washing the mouth, nose, and body once. (168) And washing the inside of the prepuce which can be retracted without difficulty, the navel, and any open piercing. And absolutely washing the braided hair of a man if water reaches its roots, and the skin of the beard, mustache, eyebrows, and the external private parts.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage enumerates the obligatory elements (fara'id) of ghusl according to the Hanafi school. The text opens by stating that there are eleven obligatory acts in ghusl, then lists them in detail. The first three—washing the mouth, nose, and the entire body once—are derived from the Quranic command to 'purify yourselves thoroughly' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6). The remaining eight obligations involve specific body parts that must be washed: the inside of the foreskin (prepuce) if it can be easily retracted, the navel cavity, any non-closed piercing (e.g., an ear piercing that has not healed shut), the roots of a man's braided hair (provided water reaches the roots), and the external skin under the beard, mustache, and eyebrows, as well as the external genitals. The text notes that for women, braided hair does not require washing if water reaches the roots; this is based on a hadith. The proofs for these rulings are provided in the commentary that follows, citing Quranic verses and hadith reports, such as the hadith that whoever leaves a hair's breadth dry in ghusl will be punished. The underlying principle is that every part of the body that is considered 'external' must be wetted, unless there is genuine hardship (like retracting a tight prepuce). This passage is a standard Hanafi ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
فرائض الغسل (fara'id al-ghusl): The obligatory acts that must be performed for a valid ritual bath (ghusl).
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water, a fard in ghusl.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose, a fard in ghusl.
قلفة (qulfah): The prepuce (foreskin); its inside must be washed if it can be retracted without difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires eleven specific obligatory acts in ghusl; omission of any invalidates the purification.

Washing Hidden Body Parts in Ghusl: Prepuce, Navel, and Piercings
Ruling with proof on hidden body parts in ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing the prepuce, navel, and open piercings in ghusl, and apply the proof from the hadith of Ali.

Core Idea
Every part of the outer skin must be washed in ghusl, including hidden areas like the prepuce and navel.

Ghusl requires water to reach every part of the outer body. But what about the inside of the prepuce, the navel, or a piercing? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on these areas, supported by hadith evidence from the Prophet ﷺ indicating that even a hair's breadth left dry invalidates the ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The text specifies three parts: inside of the prepuce (if easily retractable), navel, and an open (not closed) piercing. The ruling is that washing these is obligatory (fard) in ghusl.
The ruling is conditional: it applies only if there is no undue hardship.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites the hadith from Ali (Sunan Abi Dawud): 'Whoever leaves a spot the size of a hair from janabah without washing it, such and such will be done to him from the Fire.' This establishes the principle that no part of the skin may remain dry.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is considered categorical (qat'i al-dalalah).
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'place the size of a hair' indicates that even the smallest dry area invalidates ghusl. Hence, all parts, including hidden ones like the prepuce and navel, must be washed.
The Hanafi school uses this to require rinsing the mouth and nose as well, since those are outer body.
4
Apply the condition of difficulty
The commentary explains that if retracting the prepuce is difficult or causes hardship, washing inside is not obligatory. Similarly, if a piercing has closed over, it is excused. This is based on the principle of 'mashaqqa' (hardship).
The condition is derived from the general legal maxim: 'Hardship brings ease.'
5
Note the epistemological weight and school position
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school. Some Shafi'is consider these areas recommended rather than obligatory, but the Hanafis hold them as fard based on the explicit hadith.
The difference stems from how each school interprets the scope of 'body' in the obligation of ghusl.

Source Text
