فصل في فرائض الغسل (۱۸) وداخل قلفة لا عسر فى فسخها وسرة وثقب غير منضم خوب خوب پاکی حاصل کرو اور یہ اس وقت ہو سکتا ہے کہ کلی کر کے اور ناک میں پانی ڈال کر ہر جگہ پانی پہنچایا جائے۔ اس لئے کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا غسل میں فرض ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن علی قال ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من ترک موضع شعرة من جنابة لم يغسلها فعل بها كذا كذا من النار (ابوداؤ د شریف، باب في الغسل من الجنابة ص ۴۶، نمبر ۲۴۹) معلوم ہوا کہ ایک بال برابر بھی غسل میں خشک رہ جائے تو غسل نہیں ہوگا اسی لئے کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا ضروری ہے۔(۳) عن ابي هريرة ان النبي عل الله جعل المضمضة والاستنشاق للجنب ثلاثا فريضة (سنن دارقطنی ، باب ماروى فى مضمضة والاستنشاق في غسل الجنابة ، ج اول ص ۱۲۱، نمبر ۴۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنبی پر کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا فرض ہے۔ (۴) پورے جسم پر پانی پہنچانے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ اخبرنا ابن عباس عن خالته ميمونة قالت وضعت للنبي علم غسلا يغتسل به من الجنابة فأكفأ الاناء على يده اليمنى فغسلها مرتين او ثلاثا ثم صب على فرجه فغسل فرجه بشماله ثم ضرب بيده الارض فغسلها ثم تمضمض و استنشق و غسل وجهه و يديه ثم صب على راسه و جسده ثم تنحى ناحية فغسل رجليه - ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الغسل من الجنابة، ص ۴۵، نمبر ۲۴۵ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فى الغسل من الجنابة ، ص ،۲۸، نمبر ۱۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے وضو کرتے ، پھر فرج کو دھوتے ، پھر مضمضہ اور استنشاق کرتے پھر پورے بدن پر پانی بہاتے ۔
ترجمه : (۱۶۸) [۴] اور قلفہ کے اندر دھونا جس کے کھولنے میں تکلیف نہ ہو۔ [۵] اور ناف کے اندر دھونا۔ [4] اور اس سوراخ کا دھونا جو ملا ہوا نہ ہو۔ تشریح : اگر قلفہ کٹا ہوا نہ ہو، اور اس میں جنابت کی منی ہو، اور چمڑا پیچھے ہٹا کر آسانی سے دھو یا جاسکتا ہو تو اس کو دھونا فرض ہے ، کیونکہ وہ جسم کے باہر کا حصہ ہے ، اور اگر اس کو دھونا مشکل ہو تو دھونا فرض نہیں ہے، کیونکہ مجبوری ہے ۔ ناف کی چمڑی میں پانی پہچانا ضروری ہے، تاکہ سوکھا نہ رہ جائے ۔ سوراخ مل گیا ہو تب تو مجبوری ہے، لیکن اگر ملا ہوا نہ ہو تو اس میں بھی پانی پہنچانا ضروری ہے، کیونکہ وہ باہر کا حصہ ہے۔
وجه : (ا) عن عائشة قـالـت كان رسول الله له اذا اراد ان يغتسل من الجنابة بدأ بكفيه فغسلهما ثم غسل مرافعه و افاض عليه الماء فاذا انقاهما اهوى بهما الى حائط - (ابوداود شریف ، باب في الغسل من الجنابة ، ص ۴۵، نمبر (۲۴۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مرافع، یعنی میل کچیل کی جگہ صاف کرے۔ (۲) عن عائشة .... فيغسل فرجه و قال مسدد : يفرغ على شماله ـ و ربما كنت عن الفرج - ثم يتوضأ وضوئه للصلاة ثم يدخل يديه في الاناء
Section on Obligations of Ghusl. (18) And the inside of the prepuce which there is no difficulty in retracting, and the navel, and a piercing that is not closed. (Urdu: Achieve thorough purification. And this can be done by rinsing the mouth and putting water in the nose, reaching water to every place. Therefore rinsing the mouth and putting water in the nose are obligatory in ghusl.) (2) In a hadith: 'Ali said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: Whoever leaves a spot the size of a hair from janabah without washing it, such and such will be done to him from the Fire. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 46, no. 249) It is known that if even a hair's breadth remains dry in ghusl, the ghusl is not valid. Therefore rinsing the mouth and putting water in the nose are necessary. (3) From Abu Hurairah that the Prophet ﷺ made rinsing the mouth and sniffing water three times an obligation for the junub. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Bab ma Ruwiya fi al-Madamad wa al-Istinshaq fi Ghusl al-Janabah, vol. 1, p. 121, no. 403) This hadith states that rinsing the mouth and putting water in the nose are obligatory for the junub. (4) The proof for pouring water over the entire body is this hadith: Ibn Abbas informed us from his aunt Maimunah who said: I placed water for the Prophet ﷺ to perform ghusl from janabah. He poured water from the vessel onto his right hand and washed it twice or thrice, then poured water over his private parts and washed his private parts with his left hand, then struck his hand on the ground and washed it, then rinsed his mouth and sniffed water, washed his face and hands, then poured water over his head and body, then moved aside and washed his feet. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 45, no. 245; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 28, no. 103) This hadith shows that he first performed wudu, then washed his private parts, then did madmadah and istinshaq, then poured water over his entire body.
Translation: (168) [4] And washing inside the prepuce that can be retracted without difficulty. [5] And washing inside the navel. [4] And washing a piercing that is not closed. Explanation: If the prepuce is not circumcised and there is seminal fluid from janabah in it, and the skin can be easily retracted and washed, then washing it is obligatory because it is part of the outer body. If washing it is difficult, it is not obligatory due to constraint. Water must reach the skin of the navel so that it does not remain dry. If the piercing is closed, it is a constraint, but if it is not closed, water must reach it because it is an outer part.
Evidence: (a) From Aishah: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ, when he wanted to perform ghusl from janabah, would start with his hands, wash them, then wash his armpits (marafiq/places of dirt), and pour water over them. When they were clean, he would lean them toward the wall. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 45, no. 243) This hadith indicates washing armpits or dirty places. (2) From Aishah: ... he washed his private parts. Musaddad said: He would pour water over his left hand, and perhaps I would [do something] regarding the private part. Then he would perform wudu like for prayer, then put his hands into the vessel.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on specific parts of the body that must be washed during ghusl. The author begins by stating the matn from the main text (likely from Nur al-Idah or similar): washing inside the prepuce (if easily retractable), the navel, and any open piercing is obligatory. The Urdu commentary explains that the prepuce must be retracted if possible; otherwise it is excused. The navel must be washed so no area remains dry. For piercings, if closed they are excused; if open, water must enter. The author then provides hadith proofs: a hadith from Ali warning that leaving even a hair's breadth dry incurs punishment, establishing the principle of thoroughness. Hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet made madmadah and istinshaq obligatory for the junub. Hadith from Maimunah describing the Prophet's ghusl, showing the sequence including washing the entire body. Another hadith from Aishah mentions washing armpits. These hadiths collectively support the obligation to wash every part of the outer skin, including hidden areas like the prepuce and navel. The Hanafi position is that these parts are obligatory to wash because they are considered outer body (zahir al-badan). The authority weight from the matn is presumably Zahir al-Riwayah, and the proofs strengthen it.

Key Terms
قلفة (qulfa): The foreskin covering the glans that is cut during circumcision; the text specifies its inner part.
سرة (surra): The navel; the indentation in the abdomen.
ثقب (thaqb): A piercing or hole in the body; the text distinguishes between open (ghayr munjadhim) and closed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is recommended (mustahab) but not obligatory.
B) It is obligatory (fard) because it is part of the outer body.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires washing every part of the outer skin in ghusl, including the inside of the prepuce (if easy), navel, and any open piercing, based on the hadith warning against leaving even a hair's breadth dry.
